which it is being provided, to release it only to employees requiring such information, and not to release
or disclose it to any other party. Upon request, recipient will return the Material together with all copies
and modifications, if any, to LexisNexis Risk Solutions.
LexisNexis Risk Solutions shall not be liable for technical or editorial errors or omissions contained
herein. The information in this publication is subject to change without notice and is provided “as-is”
without a warranty of any kind. Nothing herein should be construed as constituting a warranty, as any
applicable warranty is exclusively contained in your signed agreement with LexisNexis Risk Solutions.
All names, addresses, birth dates or other identifying information in the text, or on the sample reports
and screens shown in this document, are of fictitious persons and entities and have been created for
illustrative purposes only. Any similarity to the name of any real person, school, business, other entity,
address, date of birth, or other identifying information is purely coincidental.
Due to the nature and origin of public record information, the public records and commercially available
data sources used in reports may contain errors.
The products and services discussed in this guide are not provided by “consumer reporting agencies,”
as that term is defined in the Fair Credit Reporting Act (15 U.S.C. 1681, et seq.) (FCRA), and do not
constitute “consumer reports,” as that term is defined in the FCRA. Accordingly, the products and
services discussed in this guide may not be used in whole or in part as a factor in determining eligibility
for credit, insurance, employment or for any other eligibility purpose that would qualify it as a consumer
report under the FCRA.

CONFIDENTIAL

Chapter 1

Br i d ger Insight XG
LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) is a risk management solution that lets you use search services
to compare your input entities against public and proprietary data. This functionality helps you reduce
compliance costs and protect yourself from regulatory and reputational risk.
You tell XG which settings to use to perform the search and how to manage the alerts that are
generated.
You can complete case management and workflow actions on alerts and manage batch runs. A batch run
contains the details about a batch search or an alert import and any associated alerts. You can query,
view, update, and delete alerts that are stored in the XG database. For example, you can change the alert
assignment or add an alert to an accept list. You can create reports to help you manage your XG system.
You can also use accept lists and custom screening lists in your XG processing. Accept lists can help you
suppress list screening matches in new searches that you have already processed and determined to be
false positives or help you monitor changes to entity information. Custom screening lists can help you
flag entities in list screening searches that are unique to your organization.
In addition, XG lets you use web services to integrate certain product functionality into your existing
systems.

Search Capabilities
XG offers the flexibility to search information for several entity types that you can provide in various data
formats.
You can search a business or an individual in real-time by entering the entity data into search fields in XG.
You can also search batch files that contain multiple parsed records or that contain multiple unparsed
text strings. You can upload files through the XG interface or place files in Automatic Batch folders
located on the batch servers.
Parsed data is separated into defined fields. Parsed data lets XG to process similar information in the
same manner for more relevant results.
You use batch formats that you create in XG to search input records that contain business entities,
individual entities, unknown entities, or text entities. You can also use default formats to search payment
transaction records. The following types of payment transaction data can be searched:

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 11

CONFIDENTIAL

ACH (Automated Clearing House)
For information about ACH record content and format, see https://www.nacha.org. For information
about supported ACH formats and the data that is processed by XG, see the ACH Reference Data
document that is available on the LexisNexis® Risk Solutions Customer Support Hub at https://
lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2093.
Fedwire
For information about Fedwire record content and format, see https://www.frbservices.org. For
information about Fedwire file processing in XG, see the related article that is available on
the Customer Support Hub at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2148 or https://
lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/3473.
ISO (International Organization for Standardization) 20022
For information about ISO 20022 record content and format, see http://www.iso20022.org. For
information about ISO 20022 file processing in XG, see the related article that is available on the
Customer Support Hub at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2064.
SWIFT (Society for Worldwide Interbank Financial Telecommunication)
For information about SWIFT record content and format, see http://www.swift.com.
For information about SWIFT file processing in XG, see the related article on the
Customer Support Hub at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/1883 or https://
lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2635.
Unparsed data is not separated into defined fields. You use the default XG - Unstructured batch format to
search unparsed data. A text record contains one required field of unparsed text and optional ID fields.
To search data that is not well parsed, XG looks at text strings in the files one string at a time. This type of
searching yields different results than when you search a parsed file with defined fields.
You can also search input records through XG web services. If you save these alerts to the database, then
they can be accessed for review at a later time.
XG provides numerous search options that affect the data that is searched and the searches that are
reported. You create predefined searches that tell XG which available options to use when you search
your input information. For example, you can tell XG which screening lists to search and the match
confidence score that potential matches must meet before XG creates a result.
Related Information
Real-Time Searches on page 36
Batch Searches on page 116
Predefined Searches on page 251

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 12

CONFIDENTIAL

List Screening
The list screening service supports input entity searches against LexisNexis® FCC (financial crimes
compliance) risk data. The service uses the LexisNexis® Search Core to compare the data and find
potential matches. The search results include match information and a match confidence score.
Users can view the screening lists that are available to the XG client instance. Users can view the
date that each available screening list was updated by the source agency and the date each available
screening list was updated in the XG client instance.
You can also create the following lists for more powerful processing:
• Accept lists can reduce recurring false positive matches based on the name and unique identifier
matches that were reported in previous searches. This feature uses fuzzy logic matching on multiple
data elements between the input information and the list record. This feature can also monitor data
changes that may affect previous match decisions.
• The White List uses Automatic False Positive rules to reduce recurring false positives that are based
on the name matches that were reported in previous searches. This feature uses word-for-word
matching between the input name or the input text string and the entity name or the AKA (also
known as) name in a list record.
• Custom screening lists can be used to search entities that your organization specifically wants to
monitor.
Related Information
Accept Lists on page 159
White List on page 171
Custom Screening Lists on page 175

AML Insight Service
You can use LexisNexis® AML Insight™ to conduct enhanced due diligence on businesses and individuals.
This single, easy-to-use, online resource can authenticate identities, assess financial risk, monitor
interdiction lists, and examine assets and relationships.

FraudPoint Score Service
LexisNexis® FraudPoint® Score is a highly-efficient scoring and identity data solution that greatly
enhances your ability to predict and prevent fraud and helps you identify and approve profitable
customers.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 13

CONFIDENTIAL

InstantID Service
LexisNexis® InstantID® is a search service that you can integrate into XG. The search service is a powerful
identity authentication solution that helps you prevent fraud and identity theft before they strike your
organization.

Driver's Privacy Protection Act
Users must set a DPPA (Driver’s Privacy Protection Act) permissible use for each individual search against
LexisNexis® FraudPoint® or InstantID.

with your response herein and you agree to indemnify, defend, and hold harmless LexisNexis Risk
Solutions from any breach of such certification by you, your agents, or contacts and any damages,
fees, and costs associated therewith. Information from this file may not be used to determine a
customer's eligibility for credit, insurance, or employment pursuant to the Fair Credit Reporting
Act, (15 USC Sec. 1681).
Users can set one of the following possible DPPA permissible uses. The service searches against driver
licenses, motor vehicle registrations, and boat registrations for the states that recognize the permissible
use that you set. If you set No Permissible Use, the service does not search driver licenses, motor vehicle
registrations, or boat registrations.

Alert Processing
XG generates an alert when results are returned for an input entity that you search. You can complete
various actions to process the alerts.
By default, XG does not generate an alert if the input entity is searched only against screening lists, and
no potential matches are reported.
Searches in real-time, batch, or web services can generate alerts. Real-time alerts are assigned to the
user who performed the search, to a particular user, or to a particular role. Alert assignment is set
in the predefined search. Batch alerts and web service alerts are assigned to a particular user or to a
particular role. Alert assignment is set when the search is performed. When you assign alerts to a role,
you let multiple users process alerts from an alert pool at the same time. This method may help your
organization process results more efficiently.
You access alerts by performing a query of the XG database. You can use a saved query, or you can
create a new query. You use workflow and case management features to process the alerts. You can also
import, export, and delete alerts.

Client Instance Setup on page 22
Search Capabilities on page 11

Page Elements
XG uses several standard page elements. The functionality of these page elements is the same regardless
of where the page elements are displayed in the product.

Dates
You can use dates to limit the information that is returned.
You can use the following methods to set the date:

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 17

CONFIDENTIAL

Date Fields
Calendars are used to indicate a date or a date range. You can manually enter the date, or you can select
the date from the pop-up calendar. If you leave the date blank, then the product uses the current date.
You can use the following methods to select the date:
• Click the month. A list of months appear that you can select. To change the year, click the left arrow
or the right arrow.
• Click the left arrow to view the previous month, or click the right arrow to view the next month.
• Click a day on the calendar to select that date.
• Click Today to select the current date.

Date List
The date list is used to select a predefined date range. You can also use the date list to specify a custom
date range. All times refer to the user's computer time. You can use the following options to select a date
range:
Current Week
This option ranges from Sunday of the current week at 00:00 to the end of the upcoming Saturday.
Current Month
This option ranges from the first day of the current month at 00:00 to the end of the last day of the
current month.
Previous Month
This option ranges from the same date as the current day in the previous month to the end of the
current day.
Previous 6 Months
This option ranges from the same date as the current day six months previously to the end of the
current day.
Previous 12 Months
This option ranges from the same date as the current day in the previous year to the end of the
current day.
Previous Year
This option ranges from the first day of the previous year to the end of the last day of the previous
year.
Current Year
This option ranges from the beginning of the current year to the end of the current day.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 18

CONFIDENTIAL

Custom
This option lets you set the date range.

Find
Some pages include a find option in the upper-right corner.
If you know the name of the item that you want to find, then you can enter the item name to reduce the
number of available items.
For example, you may want to find a user named Administrator 1. Instead of scrolling through the user
list, you can search for admin. XG returns any users who have a name that contains admin. If you enter
Administrator 1, then XG may return even fewer users.

Column Sort
The sort arrows are displayed in column headings when sorting is available.
You click the column title to sort. You click the column title a second time to sort in the opposite order.
The sort icons indicate the available sorting options:
indicates that the column is not sorted but is available for sorting.
indicates that the column is sorted in ascending order (A to Z, smallest to largest, or oldest to
newest).
•
indicates that the column is sorted in descending order (Z to A, largest to smallest, or newest to
oldest).

•
•

Dialog Boxes
On some pages in XG, you click a button to make a selection and a dialog box appears. Dialog boxes
display a list of the available options for the setting.
Dialog boxes can contain a find option. You can use the find option to reduce the number of available
items.
At the top of a dialog box, a message displays the total number of items in the list and the number of
the items you are currently viewing in the list. For example, if a list has 25 items, then the message may
display “11–20 of 25.” You can click to scroll to the next page or click to scroll to the previous page.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 19

CONFIDENTIAL

Some dialog boxes allow you to select only one item in the list. When you click an item in the list, the
dialog box closes and the selected item is displayed on the page. If you open the dialog box again, then
the item you selected has a check mark next to it. You can change the selected item by clicking a new
item.
Some dialog boxes allow you to select multiple items in the list. When you click items in the list, a check
mark appears next to each selection. If you click an item that already has a check mark next to it, then
the check mark is cleared. Some dialog boxes have an option to click a Select All button to select all
items in the list, or click a Deselect All button to clear all items in the list. XG remembers your selections
as you move from page to page in the dialog box.
When you finish making your selections from a dialog box, click OK to confirm your selections and close
the dialog box.

Items Per Page
In most lists, you can select the number of items that you want to appear on each page. Click the down
arrow in the field and select an option. Increase the items per page to increase your options when you
delete records or export records.

Multi-Selecting
In certain product areas, you can select multiple items in a list or a field.

Multi-Selecting in a List
Multi-selecting in a list is available when there are check boxes next to each item in a list. You can use
the following methods to select items:
• Select the check box next to the item.
• Select the check box in the heading to select all the items on the page.
• Select the check box in the heading to clear all the selected items on the page.

Multi-Selecting in a Field
Multi-selecting in a field is available when there is a check box in the field. You can use the following
methods to select items:
•
•
•
•

Click the field, and select an item.
Click the field, and enter the name of the item.
Select the check box to select all the items.
Clear the check box to clear all the selected items in the field.

About This Publication
This publication provides conceptual information and instructions about how to perform product tasks.

Audience
Personnel who have a strong understanding of the needs of your organization and have the
responsibility to set up the product should read this content.
Personnel who need to know how to perform searches and how to process results should read the
appropriate sections of this content.

Content
This content is organized in a functional way. Each section focuses on a different element of the product
and how to use it.
The content is presented with the assumption that users have full access to XG. However, users at
your organization may have limited access to functionality due to the product settings or to user access
restrictions. User access can be limited to specific areas of the product, specific lists or alerts, or specific
tasks.

Conventions
This publication uses various conventions to provide information in a standardized format.

action.

may not be optimal.

The client machines are not required to have a specific web browser.
LexisNexis Risk Solutions has tested the following web browsers:
• Microsoft Edge (current version at the time of testing)
• Google Chrome (current version at the time of testing)
• Mozilla Firefox (current version at the time of testing)
You may use a web browser that LexisNexis Risk Solutions has not tested, but your experience may
not be optimal.
Multiple sessions (additional tabs) in the same browser instance are not supported.

Open your web browser.

2.

Go to the product web address.

3.

To change the language that is displayed, select your language at the top of the page.

For systems that use MFA (multi-factor authentication), complete the following steps:
a. Enter your credentials, and click Next.
b. Enter your password, and click Next.
To change your credentials, click Change Client and User. Passwords are case sensitive. You can
reset your password if you have forgotten it.
c. If a code is required, then enter the email verification code (the OTP (one-time password)) that
the product sent to the email address that is associated with your user account.
If you do not receive the email, then verify that the email is not in your junk mail or your spam
folder. To have the product send you a new code, click (Resend Verification Code).
d. Click Next.

5.

Click Sign In.

6.

If you are the first user to sign in, then accept the EULA (end user license agreement), and click
Continue.

You are prompted to change your password the first time that you sign in and after intervals that your
organization can configure. You can change your password at any time. Your product administrator can
require you to change your password the next time that you sign in.
A password is case sensitive and needs to meet the following requirements:
•
•
•
•
•

Your password must be 8–20 characters.
Your password must contain letters and numbers.
Your password must contain at least one special character (!, @, #, $, %, &, or *).
Your password cannot contain your user ID or the reverse of your user ID.
Your password cannot repeat any of the previous 12 passwords.

Your password can expire in 1–60 days. Your organization controls the expiration requirements and the
password length requirements.
Related Information
Security Policy on page 243

Change Your Password
You can change your password at any time.
Procedure:

1.

Click your user name at the top of any main product page, and click Edit My Profile.

2.

Click Change Password.

3.

Enter your current password.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 32

CONFIDENTIAL

4.

Enter and confirm your new password.

5.

Click Save New Password.

Related Information
Passwords on page 32

Homepage
You can set a homepage as the first page you view each time that you sign in. You can select a predefined
search for real-time searches or alert query as your homepage.

Set Your Homepage
The homepage is the first product page that is displayed after you sign in. The homepage can be set to
the results of a specified alert query or to a real-time search with a specified predefined search.
Procedure:

1.

To set a real-time search that has a specific predefined search set as your homepage, complete the
following steps:
a. On the main menu, point to Search, and click the predefined search.
b. Click Make This My Homepage at the bottom of the page.

2.

To set an alert query as your homepage, complete the following steps:
a. On the main menu, point to Alerts, and click the alert query.
b. Click Make This My Homepage at the bottom of the page.

3.

To set a new alert query as your homepage, complete the following steps:
a. On the main menu, point to Alerts, and click New Query.
b. Create the query that you want as your homepage.
c. Click Find Records.
d. Click Make This My Homepage at the bottom of the page.
This query is not considered a saved query. The query is not retained if you change your
homepage.

and maintain access to sensitive data. This data includes an individual's SSN (Social Security number),

You can also view the terms and conditions and the privacy policy from links at the bottom of each main
product page.

Chapter 3

R ea l - Ti me Search es
A real-time search lets you select a predefined search and manually search input entity information in
the LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) application.
You can limit the access to the alert to a particular division. You can set only divisions that you belong to.
Only the users who belong to the selected division can access the alert. The predefined search may set
the alert to be assigned to another user or role. In this case, you can set only a division that both you and
the user belong to or that both you and at least one user in the role belongs to.
The search fields that XG displays are controlled by the default fields that are set for the system or by the
fields that are set for the predefined search.
After you perform a real-time search, one of the following events occur:
• The alert is assigned to you and the results are displayed.
• A message indicates that the alert is assigned to another user or role.
• A message prompts you to download a report because an alert was not generated.
Related Information
Input Fields for Real-Time Searches on page 38
Predefined Searches on page 251
Divisions on page 240
Real-Time Searches Report on page 210

Perform a Real-Time Search
You perform a real-time search to manually search a single individual or business.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 36

CONFIDENTIAL

To view a training video about this task, see the training that is available on the LexisNexis® Risk
Solutions Customer Support at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Search, and click the predefined search that you want to use.
Predefined searches are available for a search if they meet the following criteria:
• The entity type of the input data is supported by the selected search services.
• The input data meets the requirements of the selected search services.
• The user has access to the predefined search based on division access and role access.

2.

Depending on the search services that are selected in the predefined search, select a GLBA
(Gramm-Leach-Bliley Act) permissible use.

3.

Depending on the search services that are selected in the predefined search, select a DPPA (Driver’s
Privacy Protection Act) permissible use.

4.

Select the division access.
This field displays only the divisions that you belong to. This field is not available if you belong to
only one division. If the selected predefined search is set to assign the alert to another user or to
roles, then the field shows only the divisions that both you and the assigned user belongs to or that
both you and at least one user in one of the assigned roles belongs to.

5.

If the selected predefined search can be used for more than one type of entity, then select the
entity type of your input entity.

6.

Depending on your predefined search, click Show First Last Name or Show Full Name to display the
name fields that you want to use.

7.

To add fields to the search, click Add Fields, and select the field group.

8.

To remove a field group, click

9.

Enter your input entity information.

(Delete) next to the field group.

10. Click Search.
11. If an alert is not generated and you want a record of the search, then click Print Report.
“No match” results are typically not stored in the database. To keep a record of the search,
generate the report.
Related Information
Predefined Searches on page 251
Divisions on page 240
Real-Time Searches Report on page 210
Input Fields for Real-Time Searches on page 38

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 37

CONFIDENTIAL

Input Fields for Real-Time Searches
To perform real-time searches, you must enter a name for the input entity. Depending on the selected
predefined search, you may be required to enter additional information. You may also be able to provide
additional information as needed. The format for date fields is determined by your browser settings.
Related Information
Additional Information Fields on page 38
Name and Gender Fields on page 39
ID Fields on page 40
Address and Location Fields on page 48
Phone Fields on page 50
Real-Time Searches on page 36

Additional Information Fields
The input fields that are available vary for real-time searches, batch searches, or custom screening list
records. The entity type also affects the available fields.
The following table lists the fields alphabetically and indicates when the field is available by purpose and
entity type.
Table legend:
• I = Individual
• B = Business

• T = Text
• U = Unknown

• V = Vessel
• C = Country

When single records are directly added to custom screening lists, additional Comments fields are
available for various data elements.
For certain IDs, fields other than the Number field are not applicable due to the nature of the ID. These
fields are available only for single records that are directly added to custom screening lists.
The Date of Birth field and the Citizenship fields are displayed with identifications for real-time
searches.

Number, Street Name, Street Number, Street Type, and Sub Building Number.

Chapter 4

Alerts
LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) generates an alert when a search returns results. By default, the
product does not generate an alert if the input entity is only searched against the list screening service
and no potential matches are reported.
Alerts that were generated from real-time searches and batch searches performed through the XG
interface are stored in the XG database. You can also choose to store alerts that were generated from
Automatic Batch searches and XG web services in the database.
Each alert contains the following information:
•
•
•
•

The alert information that you can use to help guide alerts through your review process
The search service results that were returned
The record details of the alert, which includes the account information and the input information
The record history of actions that were taken on the alert

Consolidating this information into a single record helps you to process your results, or perform case
management, more efficiently. You review the information in the alert. XG highlights the information
that matched. Based on your organization’s policies and training, you take action on the result.

Alert Information
The Alert Information section displays the following information:
•
•
•
•

The status that indicates the current stage of your review process for the alert
The alert assignment that indicates which user or users in a role need to process the alert
The state (Open or Closed) that indicates whether the alert needs further processing
The ID number that is used to identify the alert in the XG database

Search Input
The Search Input section is only available for the classic alert view. In the new alert view, the search input
is included in the list screening results. The section displays the following input entity information:
• Name of the entity, or text string context, or match text (specific data in the context that matched the
input entity) of the payment data or the unstructured data
• Address
• SSN (Social Security number) or EIN (employer identification number)
• Phone number
• DOB (date of birth)

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 52

CONFIDENTIAL

The current work phone number is displayed for businesses. Only one phone number is displayed for
individuals. XG uses the following priority order to determine the phone number that is displayed:
current phone number, current work phone number, and then previous home phone number.
Only one address is displayed. XG uses the following priority order to determine the address that is
displayed: current address, mailing address, and then previous address.
Related Information
Alert Processing on page 77
Alert Viewing on page 78
List Screening Results in the Classic Alert View on page 59

Results
An alert contains any results that are returned from each search service that is searched. The alert also
contains any results that are returned from any search that is added after the initial search is performed.
Alerts can contain results from the following search services:
• List Screening
XG displays the results differently depending on which alert view you select.
• LexisNexis® FraudPoint® Score
• LexisNexis® InstantID®
All clients can view alerts in the new alert view, which features a redesigned page and additional
functionality (for example, match notes and the history of duplicate automatic false positives).
Some legacy clients also have access to the classic alert view.
Related Information
Record Details on page 75
Record History on page 76

List Screening Results in the New Alert View
An alert can contain up to 500 potential matches against screening lists that are provided by LexisNexis
Risk Solutions and up to 500 potential matches against custom screening lists.
In the list screening results of the alert, XG first displays the input entity and then the list entities that
were reported as matches. The entity information that is displayed is based on the specified field set.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 53

CONFIDENTIAL

If match decisions were configured in the predefined search, then you can set the decision for each
entity. Match decision options are not available for true match updates.
You can also expand each match to view the profile data, the list entity information, and the match
notes. You can add or edit the match notes. Match notes are available in only the PDF version of the List
Screening Report.

P r o f i l e Data
For each match, XG provides profile data about the input entity, the list entity, and the match results.
This profile data summarizes the match.
The following result information is provided for the match:
• Profile picture
• List entity name
• Profile ID
The profile ID, also called a proprietary UID (user identification number), is a unique ID that LexisNexis
Risk Solutions generates for the list entity. This ID is not the LexID® number.
• Match summary
®

A profile picture may be provided only for matches against the LexisNexis WorldCompliance
Data Plus list.

™

Match Summary
The match summary provides information in a table format about the input entity, the list entity, and the
search core analysis.
Context information from payment transaction searches or unstructured searches is displayed as
a name.
If the match is a true match update or a false match update, then a message is displayed at the top of
the section.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 54

CONFIDENTIAL

For the list entity, the match summary uses the following icons to indicate whether the data element was
a match:
•

(highly likely match)

•

(somewhat likely match)

•

(less likely match)

The search core analysis may indicate whether the data element was a match or lists the match
confidence score.
Depending on the entity type, the following information is provided for the match:
Business Entities
For business entities, the following input information may be provided in the match summary:
• Entity type
• Entity name
For the entity names in the list record, the table may indicate the type of entity, AKA (also known
as), or native script.
• ID numbers
For the ID numbers in the list record, the table may indicate the ID type, the associated country,
the issue date, or the issuer.
• Addresses
For addresses in the list record, the table may indicate the address type or country association
type.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 55

CONFIDENTIAL

Individual or Unknown Entities
For individual or unknown entities, the following input information may be provided in the match
summary:
• Entity type
• Entity name
For the entity names in the list record, the table may indicate the type of entity, AKA, or native
script.
• Date of birth
• Gender
• ID numbers
For the ID numbers in the list record, the table may indicate the ID type, the associated country,
the issue date, or the issuer.
• Address
For addresses in the list record, the table may indicate the address type or country association
type.
• Place of Birth
• Citizenship

L i s t E n t i t y I n fo rmat ion
For each match, XG provides the list entity information from the record that contained the match.
This information includes screening list information and comments. For matches against screening
lists that are provided by LexisNexis Risk Solutions, legacy LexisNexis® WorldCompliance™ lists, and
custom screening lists, entity data is also provided as additional information. For matches against
the WorldCompliance Data Plus list, entity data is also provided by segment and for relationships. In
addition, record sources are provided.
Screening List Information
For each match, XG provides information from the list record that contained the match.
The screening list information includes the list name, the date that the list file was built, the date that
the record was created, and the date that the record was last updated.
In addition, the reason that the entity was listed may be provided for only matches against screening lists
that are provided by LexisNexis Risk Solutions, legacy WorldCompliance lists, and custom screening lists.
In addition, the position and entity status may be provided only for matches against the
WorldCompliance Data Plus list.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 56

CONFIDENTIAL

When XG determines that the match is an automatic false positive, the following information is
displayed:
• The false positive confidence score that XG determined for the match, which is based on the specified
rules for LexisNexis® Intelligent Match Decision Solution (IMDS)
This score indicates how confident the rules are that the match is a false positive. The score can range
from 0.0000 (no confidence of a false positive) to 10.0000 (full confidence of a false positive).
This value is not the same as the match confidence score (70–100) that XG determines for each
match to indicate how likely that the input entity is a possible match.
• The reason codes that were returned for the match, which are based on the specified rules for IMDS
• The intelligent match decision rules that were used to determine that the match was an automatic
false positive
This information is available only if rules were configured in the predefined search and used to
determine that the match was an automatic false positive.
For more information about the rules for IMDS and possible reason codes, see the Rules for LexisNexis®
Intelligent Match Decision Solution technical reference guide.
Entity Data from WorldCompliance Data Plus
For matches on the WorldCompliance Data Plus list, the entity data that is returned may include
segment data and relationships.

Segment Data
The following segment data may be returned:
Sanctions
Each sanctions listing can contain the country and the WorldCompliance source.
Enforcements
Each enforcement incident can contain the following information:
• Country
• Subcategory
• WorldCompliance source
Adverse Media
Each adverse media incident can contain the description and the subcategory.

CONFIDENTIAL

• Inactive
• Unknown

• Country
• Administrative unit
• Administrative level (for example, National)
• Subcategories
• Country role
Possible values:
• MicroPEP
• PEP
• Unknown
• Governing institution (for example, Office of the President)
• Governing role (for example, President)
• Effective date of the role
• Expiration date of the role
SOE

•
•
•
•
•
•

Status
Total ownership percentage
Subcategory
Domain
Ownership country
Ownership country percentage

Registration

Additional Segments

• Segment

Ma t ch Not es
Each match may contain up to 20 user-provided notes with information that is specifically relevant to the
match instead of the alert in general.
To help ensure users are aware of the notes, the match note field can be added to an alert view
field set as part of your administrative tasks.

List Screening Results in the Classic Alert View
An alert can contain up to 500 potential matches against screening lists that are provided by LexisNexis
Risk Solutions and up to 500 potential matches against custom screening lists.
The classic alert view is the legacy method used to separately navigate through selected alerts.
Your XG client instance may not be configured to display this view. This functionality will be retired
in the future. Be sure to become familiar with the new alert view for a seamless transition in your
review processes.
By default, XG displays the first 25 matches in the alert in the classic alert view. When you view the alert,
you can set XG to display additional matches.
Each potential match provides the following information:

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 59

CONFIDENTIAL

Decision Options
You can set the match to False Positive or True Match. These options are only available if they are
configured in the predefined search. Decision options are not available for true match updates.
Match Information
The match information includes the entity name of the list record that matches the input entity, the
match confidence score, and the list that contains the match.
Automatic False Positive
The Automatic False Positive section displays the following information:
• The false positive confidence score that XG calculated for the match, which is based on the
specified rules for IMDS
This score indicates how confident the rules are that the match is a false positive. The score
can range from 0.0000 (no confidence of a false positive) to 10.0000 (full confidence of a false
positive).
This value is not the same as the match confidence score (70–100) that XG provides for
each match to indicate how likely that the input entity is a possible match.
• The reason codes that were returned for the match, which are based on the specified rules for
IMDS
• The intelligent match decision rules that were used to determine that the match was an
automatic false positive
This information is available only if rules were configured in the predefined search and used to
determine that the match was an automatic false positive.
For more information about rules for IMDS and possible reason codes, see the rule documentation.
Match Summary
The Match Summary section displays an overview of the input entity information that matches the
list record. The following indicators are possible:
•
•
•

(exact match)
(close match)
(genders do not match)
Context information from payment searches or unstructured searches is displayed as a name.

Match Details
The match details include the list record that matches the input entity. The matching information is
highlighted. If the entry is a true match update or a false match update, then a message is displayed
at the top of the section.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 60

CONFIDENTIAL

The match details may include links to information from list sources. You can click the link to open
the corresponding website in a new browser page.
The match details may include links to the associates of the input entity. You can click the link to view
the associate information in a new browser page.

FraudPoint Score Results
FraudPoint Score results can help predict the likelihood that the applicant input information is of
unreliable authenticity, fraudulent, or materially misrepresented, and that the account would result in a
fraud loss write-off.
FraudPoint Score results include the following information:
•
•
•
•

FraudPoint Score value
For FraudPoint Score 2.0, fraud risk indices
Potential warning codes
If configured for the search, a LexisNexis® Red Flags Rule Report

For more information about the FraudPoint Score results, see the LexisNexis® FraudPoint® Score
Analyzing Results white paper that is available on the LexisNexis® Risk Solutions Customer Support
Hub at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2086.
If you view an alert in the classic alert view, then you can download the results in a FraudPoint Score
report as a PDF file.
Related Information
Alert Reports in the New Alert View on page 106

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 61

CONFIDENTIAL

R e d F l a g s Ru l e Rep ort
If configured for the search, the results include a Red Flags Rule Report. The report highlights suspicious
personal identifying information and displays warning codes when red flags risk factors are present. Red
flag alerts inform users of suspicious activity with warning conditions or red flag alerts, clearly associated
with red flags guidelines. Users are alerted to suspicious identity information (for example, a false or
disconnected telephone number, a mis-keyed or mismatched SSN, or invalid ZIP Codes.)
Red Flags
FraudPoint Score can be configured to return red flags for individual entities.
The service can return the following red flags:

Value

Description

10

Report Summary for Individual Results
The report summary lists InstantID results for individuals.
The report summary may list the following information:
•
•
•
•

If a report was requested, a link to the Red Flags Rule Report

the NAP (name, address, and phone number) result

Red Flags Rule Report
If configured for the search, the results include a Red Flags Rule Report. The report highlights suspicious
personal identifying information and displays warning codes when red flags risk factors are present. Red
flag alerts inform users of suspicious activity with warning conditions or red flag alerts, clearly associated
with red flags guidelines. Users are alerted to suspicious identity information (for example, a false or
disconnected telephone number, a mis-keyed or mismatched SSN, or invalid ZIP Codes.)

Verification Details for Individual Results
The verification details indicate which input information matched, conflicted, or was not available for
matching.
InstantID also returns possible alternate data. The following information are examples of possible
alternate data:
•
•
•
•
•

A phone number that is associated with the input name or the input address
A name or an address that is associated with the input phone number
Up to three alternate or prior addresses with mail activity dates
Up to two alternate last names that are associated with the input SSN
The SSN date of issuance ranges and state of issuance

In addition, InstantID returns corrected mistyped information. InstantID may correct minor data
discrepancies, such as a missing apartment number or transposed numbers. Corrected mistyped
information does not affect the index, but the correction may be listed as a risk indicator.
Follow-up Actions
InstantID can return follow-up actions for individual entities. For example, InstantID may suggest that
you ask the individual for a utility bill or other documentation that shows a physical address location for
an address that contains a PO Box number.
Follow-up Actions
Code

Description

A

Follow your internal policy regarding potential matches to OFAC
database information

B

Verify name with Social (via SSN card, DL if applicable, paycheck stub,
or other Government Issued ID)

C

Verify name with Address (via DL, utility bill, Directory Assistance,
paycheck stub, or other Government Issued ID)

D

Verify phone (Directory Assistance, utility bill)

E

Follow your internal policy regarding potential matches to non-OFAC
global screening lists

InstantID can return the following civil filings information for businesses:

Record Details
Each alert contains record details that list the input information that was provided in the search.
You can also view the following information related to the alert:
• The origin, or product area, from where the search was performed
This section notes if input data was truncated in a web service search.
• The date and time that the search was performed
• The predefined search that was used to generate the alert
• The division of the users who can access the alert
• The file and the format that was used for alerts that were generated from batch searches
You can change the account information for the alert. However, you cannot change or add other
identifying information to the record.
You can also attach a file or delete a file attachment. You click the attachment link to view the file. Some
files may be displayed in a browser page. Other files may prompt you to download the file.

Automatic False Positive History
XG includes an automatic false positive history in each alert if the option was configured in the alert
query.
The automatic false positive history lists the date, time, and origin of the search for which a duplicate
automatic false positive was found.
The automatic false positive history is not available in the classic alert view.

Alert Processing
XG features powerful workflow and case management functionality that you use to process alerts.
To help reduce risk, follow your organization's review processes to work through the alerts. For example,
your organization may want you to perform different actions for alerts that are generated from different
screening lists.
You can take the following actions when you view a list of alerts that meet your query criteria:
• Apply an alert decision.
• Export alerts or delete alerts.
• Generate alert processing reports.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 77

CONFIDENTIAL

You can take the following actions on a single alert when you view the record's alert details:
•
•
•
•
•
•
•
•

Attach a file or delete a file attachment.
Set match decisions.
Add match notes.
Edit account information.
Apply an alert decision.
Export the alert or delete the alert.
Add search service results.
Generate alert processing reports.

Related Information
Alerts on page 52

Alert Viewing
Users can use alert queries to view alerts in multiple ways. The method that you use to view an alert
depends on how the alert is generated and what actions you may want to take on the alert.
XG immediately displays an alert that is generated from a real-time search if the alert is assigned to the
user who performed the search. You can also perform a query to view a list of alerts that meet specific
criteria. In the query, you can customize the columns that display for the alert list. To view the details of
the selected alerts, you can view the alerts one at a time.
For alerts that are generated through batch searches or that were imported, you can also view
the alerts when you review the batch run.
Related Information
Alerts on page 52
Alert Processing on page 77
Match Notes on page 59
Add or Edit a Match Note on page 80
Batch Searches on page 116

V i e w A l e rt s
You can use alert queries to view alerts.
For alerts that are generated through batch searches or that were imported, you can also view
the alerts when you review the batch run.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 78

CONFIDENTIAL

Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Alerts, and locate alerts by using one of the following methods:
• To use a saved query to find alerts, click the query.
• To use a new query to find alerts, click New Query, and perform a query.
The Alerts page displays a list of alerts that meet the query criteria, or the page displays a list of
payment transactions that generated alerts that meet the query criteria. Alerts that other users are
currently viewing are not displayed on the page. Refresh the browser page to view new alerts or
alerts that other users were previously viewing.
You can use the browser print functionality to print the alerts on the page. You can increase the
browser page length or decrease the view percentage to view more alerts on the page.

2.

To show or hide the query criteria that was used to locate the alerts, toggle View Query.

3.

If you queried payment transactions, then click the payment transaction that contains the alerts
that you want to view.
Refresh the browser page to view new alerts or alerts that were previously being viewed by other
users.

4.

To view the details of the alerts in the list, click the alert that you want to view first.
To view the alert in the new alert view, click Try the new Alert View. To view the alert in the classic
alert view, click Switch back to the classic alert view.
The Alert View page displays the details of the alert that you clicked. You can use the navigation
toolbar to access the other alerts in the list. You can click (Next) to navigate to the next alert
unless another user is viewing that alert. After you reach the last alert in the list, you can click
(Next) to navigate to the first alert in the list.

5.

To view a particular section of the alert, expand the section.
To expand all the sections, click Show All. To collapse all the sections, click Hide All.

6.

To view the details of list matches in the new alert view, click the field set when multiple options are
available, and click each list match.
The arrow in the list match row indicates that the match can be expanded or collapsed.

7.

To view the details of list matches in the classic alert view, use the following methods:
• Click Hide All Matches to hide the details of the matches that are currently listed.
• Click Show All Matches to view the details of the matches that are currently listed.
• Click Display More Results to view the next 25 matches in the alert.
• Click Display All Results to view all matches in the alert.

Related Information
Shortcuts on page 31
Review a Batch Run on page 143
Alert Queries on page 97

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 79

CONFIDENTIAL

Match Note Management
Match notes retain user-provided information for future reference when that information is specifically
relevant to the match instead of the alert in general.
Match notes are displayed to the right of the match details in the expandable match notes section. You
can add up to 20 notes per match. You cannot delete a match note. Changes made to a note are listed in
the record history.
To help ensure users are aware of the notes, the match note field can be added to an alert view
field set as part of your administrative tasks.
Related Information
Alert View Field Sets on page 297
Set Up an Alert View Field Set on page 298

Ad d o r E d it a Matc h Note
You can add or edit a note for a list screening match when you view an alert in the alert view. This
feature is not available in the classic alert view.
Procedure:

1.

View the alert on the Alert View page.

2.

Expand the List Screening section.

3.

Click the match to display the match details.

You can attach files to alerts to support your review processes and to store external documentation in a
centralized location. For example, you can attach a scanned driver license to help create an decision trail.
The file attachment functionality is only available if your XG client instance is configured to provide this
option. You can attach the following types of files:
•

PDF

TIFF or TIF
TXT (text)
XLS or XLSX (Microsoft Excel)

In XG Service, you can attach files up to 1 MB in size. In XG Enterprise, your product administrator

You can add a note when you attach a file. Your process settings may require that you add a note. The
note that you add is displayed with the file attachment link in the record details. The note is removed if
the attachment is deleted. The note is not listed as an event in the record history.
LexisNexis News is no longer available, but results may have been attached to past alerts.

AM L I n s i g ht O verview
You can use LexisNexis® AML Insight™ to conduct enhanced due diligence on businesses and individuals.
This single, easy-to-use, online resource can authenticate identities, assess financial risk, monitor
interdiction lists, and examine assets and relationships.
You can access AML Insight when you view a single alert for a business entity or an individual entity in
XG. You cannot access the search service when you view an alert for an unknown entity or a text entity.
If the import functionality is configured, then you can export results from AML Insight and import them
as attachments to the XG alert from which you accessed the search service.
The results from FraudPoint Score and InstantID that are returned from searches are not part of
the XG workflow and case management. You can still export these results as file attachments.

CONFIDENTIAL

Ac c e p t L is t E nt ities
You can use an alert decision to add an entity that you determine is a false positive to an accept list.
Alternatively, you can add an entity that you want to monitor profile changes to an accept list. The alert
decision must be configured to let you add entities to accept lists.
Accept list records contain information that helped generate the reported match from both the input
entity and the screening list entity. However, accept lists do not contain all alert information. For
example, accept list records do not contain file attachments, the record history, or results from
other search services. Accept list records also do not store MR (machine-readable) Line 1 and Line
2 information that was provided as search input from passports or visas.
The alert must contain the following information:
• The input entity information must contain a name.
An alert may not contain an entity name if the input record was included in a batch file in which one
of the following cases is true:
• The batch file was large enough during upload to prevent missing name errors in the preview
validation from not allowing the search.
• The batch file was processed using the XG - Unstructured format.
• The batch file was processed using a payment transaction format, and the match was generated
from the text string context.
• The input record must contain a unique identifier.
The accept lists use these unique identifiers to find the matching accept list records.
Unique identifiers can be an ID number (with the exception of group ID or provider ID) or a complete
address.
If an ID number was not provided in the search, then you can add an account ID in the record
details of the alert and add the alert to an accept list. You should not provide non-unique ID numbers
because this type of data can adversely affect accept list processing.
The complete address can be made up of at least four words or numbers in the following field
combinations:
• Address Line 1, City, and State
• Address Line 1 and Postal Code
• Address Line 1, City, and Country
Alerts that are generated from batch searches that were processed with the XG - Unstructured format
cannot be added to accept lists. However, you can create White List records from this alert information.
After you add the alert to an accept list and include the accept list in predefined searches, XG does not
report the input entity as a list screening match as long as the same lists are searched and as long as the
input entity information and the screening list information have not changed significantly. Matches are
not suppressed by the accept list if changes were made to the input entity name or the unique identifier.
Matches are also not suppressed if the screening list entity name, the best-matching name, or the file
name changes.

Ap p ly a n Al ert D ecis ion to a Si ngle Re cord
You should complete all processing tasks that are needed at this stage before you apply an alert decision.
To view a training video about this task, see the training that is available on the LexisNexis® Risk
Solutions Customer Support at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s.
Before you begin this task:

The predefined search that generated the alert may require you to set decisions for each screening list
match. You must set the decisions before you can apply an alert decision that closes the alert state or
that adds the alert to an accept list.
You may want to perform the following processing actions before you apply an alert decision:
• Generate an OFAC (Office of Foreign Assets Control) report or a SAR (suspicious activity report).
• Add a file attachment.
• Add search service results.
The options that are available or required in an alert decision depend on the settings that are configured
when the alert decision is set up.

Procedure:

1.

View the alert.

2.

Click an alert decision.
Only alert decisions that you can access based on your role or your divisions are displayed. Also,
the alert decision is displayed only if access is allowed by the predefined search that generated the
alert.
In many cases, the alert decision displays its possible options. If the alert decision was set up as a
one-click application when no user input is required, then XG either remains on the alert or moves
to the next alert. XG adds an Alert Decision Applied event to the record history. XG may also
add other events if the actions were performed when the alert decision was applied.

3.

Set an assignment:
a. Select an assignment option.
b. Select a user or a role.
If you want to assign the alert to a user, then only users who belong to the division that can access
the alert are displayed.
If you want to assign the alert to a role, then only roles that have users who belong to the division
that can access the alert are displayed.

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 90

CONFIDENTIAL

Select a status.
Your process settings or list settings may require you to set a status for certain case management
actions even if the alert decision was not originally set up with this option. For example, if an alert
status is required when an alert is closed, then an alert status must be set even if the alert decision
was set to not allow a status change.

5.

Select a state.

6.

Select an accept list.
You can only add the alert to an accept list that you can access based on your divisions. Alerts that
are generated from batch searches that were processed with the XG - Unstructured format cannot
be added to an accept list. However, you can add your input names and matching list names to the
White List.

7.

Select a custom screening list:
a. Select the list.
b. Select a custom screening list reason.
c. If the input entity was searched as an unknown entity type, then identify the entity type by
selecting Persist Unknown as Individual or Persist Unknown as Business.
You can only add the alerts to a list that you can access based on your divisions. Lists that contain
country records are not available.
Alerts that are generated from batch searches that were processed with the XG - Unstructured
format cannot be added to custom screening lists.
The entity is available for searching after the list is indexed.

8.

Select decision tags.

9.

Enter a note.
Your process settings may require you to add a note for certain case management actions even if
the alert decision was not originally set up with this option.

10. To move to the next alert after you apply the alert decision, select Move to the next alert.
11. Click Apply.
Result:

XG either remains on the alert or moves to the next alert. XG adds an Alert Decision Applied event
to the record history. XG may also add other events if the actions were performed when the alert
decision was applied.
If you added an alert to a custom screening list or to an accept list and you were required to add a note,
then the note is added to the record history and the Comments field in the list record.
If you assign the alert to a user, then the user settings may set XG to send an email notification to the
assigned user.

Multiple Entity Process Management
A multiple entity process lets you monitor the status of XG applying an alert decision to alerts from the
alert list. A multiple entity process also lets you monitor the export or the import of an accept list or a
custom screening list.
You can complete the following tasks to manage processes:
• Determine whether the process is completed. You can retry processes that have a status of
Incomplete, Error, or Canceled. You can delete processes that do not have a status of Created
or In Process.
• View the process summary.
• View the alerts that were changed by the process.
• Delete a process.

Alert Queries
The XG database can be queried for alerts that meet specified criteria based on input entity information
and certain results. For example, you can query alerts based on the score that was returned for a list
match. You cannot query for the matching entity information that was returned by the search service.
XG provides various default alert queries. You can also create queries to support your risk management
program or to simplify processing tasks. Alert queries can be used one time or saved for reuse as
personal queries or shared queries.
You can create either a general query or a payment query. A general query returns a list of alerts that
meet the specified criteria. You can navigate through the list and process the alerts. A payment query
returns a list of payment transactions that generated alerts that meet the specified criteria. You select
a transaction to navigate through and process the alerts that are associated with that transaction. To
process other payment transactions, you must navigate back to the alert list or perform a new query.
Alert queries return unlocked alerts by default. However, you can choose to include alerts that are locked
by other users.
Alert query functionality is a powerful feature. Queries can be created that do not return any
alerts or to set up processes that overlook alerts. Thoroughly test queries before you implement
the queries for your organization.
Related Information
View Alerts on page 78
Account Types on page 301
Alert Statuses on page 302

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 97

CONFIDENTIAL

Default Alert Queries
XG provides default alert queries that find alerts that are assigned to you or your role.
XG provides the following default alert queries:
My Alerts
The My Alerts query returns alerts that are assigned to you. You cannot edit or delete this query.
My EFT Alerts
The My EFT Alerts query returns payment transactions that generated alerts that are assigned to
you. You cannot edit or delete this query.
My Role Alerts
The My Role Alerts query returns alerts that are assigned to your role. You can edit or delete this
query.
My EFT Role Alerts
The My EFT Role Alerts query returns payment transactions that generated alerts that are
assigned to your role. You can edit or delete this query.
Related Information
Personal Alert Queries on page 98
Query Logic on page 99

Personal Alert Queries
You can set up saved alert queries for your personal use that you do not share with other users. You
can use these alert queries to prioritize alerts based on your needs. XG uses a icon to indicate that
a saved alert query is a personal query that is only available for your use. XG does not display personal
alert queries to other users.

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 98

CONFIDENTIAL

Shared Alert Queries
You can give access to saved queries to specified roles, which can help you control which users can use
the queries. For example, you can create a saved query that finds high-priority, open alerts that must be
processed quickly. If your process involves a specific group at your organization that reviews open alerts
that have a high score, then you can create a saved query that the specific group can use to find those
alerts.

Query Logic
You must understand query logic before you can create queries to find alerts in the XG database.
An alert query can contain a combination of simple expressions, compound expressions, and complex
expressions that define the criteria that alerts must meet to be returned. You create a simple expression
by selecting the type of information that you want to find. You create a compound expression by using
“and” and “or” logical operators to join two or more simple expressions together. You create a complex
expression by using parentheses to group at least one compound expression with other expressions.
Related Information
Set Up an Alert Query on page 103
Delete Alert Queries on page 105

S i mp le E x pres sion s
Alert queries contain simple expressions. Simple expressions contain a specified field and a comparison
operator.
Many simple expressions also contain a particular value that relates to the specified field. The
comparison operator indicates how the field and the value must be related. The comparison operators
that are available depend on the selected field.
Some comparison operators set parameters for text values. The following are examples of operators for
text fields:
•
•
•
•

is
is not
contains
does not contain

This expression example searches for matches against the OFAC SDN (specially designated nationals)
screening list:
( [List Name] Is "OFAC SDN.BDF" )

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 99

CONFIDENTIAL

Some comparison operators set a parameter for numeric values. The following are examples of
operators for numeric fields:
•
•
•
•
•
•
•

is
is not
is between
is greater than
is greater than or equal to
is less than
is less than or equal to

This expression example searches for records that contain account IDs that are 1112223333:
( [Account ID] Is "1112223333" )

Some simple expressions do not require a specified value. The following are examples of operators that
do not require a specified value:
•
•
•
•
•
•
•
•

does not exist
exists
has items
is blank
matches
does not match
meet score threshold
is below score threshold

The does not exist comparison operator and the is blank comparison operator search for records
that do not contain a value in the specified field.
This expression example searches for records that contain a reason why the entity is listed on a screening
list:
( [Reason Listed] Exists )

C o m po u n d E x pres s ions
You can build alert queries and advanced automatic false positive rules that contain compound
expressions. You create a compound expression by joining simple expressions with a logical operator.
XG accepts and and or as logical operators.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 100

CONFIDENTIAL

The and operator requires that both expressions are true. This expression example searches for matches
against the OFAC SDN screening list with a match confidence score of 90 or higher:
( [List Name] Is "OFAC SDN.BDF" ) And ( [Score] Is Greater Than Or Equal To "90" )

The or operator requires that at least one of the expressions is true. This expression example searches
for matches against the OFAC SDN screening list or matches with a match confidence score of 90 or
higher:
( [List Name] Is "OFAC SDN.BDF" ) Or ( [Score] Is Greater Than Or Equal To "90" )

For some selected criteria, XG automatically builds a compound expression. You can change the
comparison operators and the logical operators that are contained within these expressions, but the
change to the expression may eliminate useful results. In some of these cases, the product displays
simplified text instead of the full compound expression.

C o m p l e x Ex pres s ions
You can build alert queries that contain complex expressions. Complex expressions consist of multiple
compound expressions and simple expressions that are grouped together with parentheses.
This expression example searches for records with a last name of Smith and an account ID of 121234 or
with a last name of Brown and an account ID of 565678:
( [Input Last Name] Is "Smith" ) And ( [Input Account ID] Is "121234" )
Or ( ( [Input Last Name] Is "Brown" ) And ( [Input Account ID] Is "565678"

) )

Date Ranges
XG uses defined date ranges to refine the alerts that are returned from a query.
You can use the following options to select a date range:
Current Week
This option ranges from Sunday of the current week at 00:00 to the end of the upcoming Saturday.
Current Month
This option ranges from the first day of the current month at 00:00 to the end of the last day of the
current month.
Previous Month
This option ranges from the same date as the current day in the previous month to the end of the
current day.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 101

CONFIDENTIAL

Previous 6 Months
This option ranges from the same date as the current day six months previously to the end of the
current day.
Previous 12 Months
This option ranges from the same date as the current day in the previous year to the end of the
current day.
Previous Year
This option ranges from the first day of the previous year to the end of the last day of the previous
year.
Current Year
This option ranges from the beginning of the current year to the end of the current day.
Custom
This option lets you set the date range.
XG uses defined date ranges in conjunction with UTC (coordinated universal time) to synchronize time
within the application to each user's locale. The UTC date is stored in the database. The time and date
displayed for each user is localized to their computer's time zone configuration.
UTC is not adjusted for daylight saving time, however, daylight saving time is reflected in the translation
relative to the user's locale.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 102

CONFIDENTIAL

Alert Reports
Alert reports can help you process and manage alerts.
The reports that are available and their possible file formats depend on how you view the alert and the
data in the alerts. Possible file formats include PDF, CSV, and Excel.

Alert Reports for Alert Lists
XG lets users generate certain reports when they view alerts in an alert list.
The following reports are available depending on the data in the alerts:
• The Alert List report lists the alerts that were returned in the query.
• The EFT Summary Report provides information about the payment transaction that generated the
alert.
• The Record Details Report provides details about the search and the alert it generated.
• The Record History Report lists the events and actions that were taken against an alert.
• The Result Summary Report displays a summary of the search service results that were returned in
the alert.

Alert Reports in the Classic Alert View
XG lets users generate certain reports when they view alerts separately in the classic alert view.
The following reports are available depending on the data in the alerts:
• The SAR (suspicious activity report) can be used to report suspicious activity for further review.
• The OFAC Report can be used to report when you determine that an input entity is a true match to an
entity on an OFAC screening list.
• The EFT Summary Report provides information about the payment transaction that generated the
alert.
• The Record Details Report provides details about the search and the alert it generated.
• The Record History Report lists the events and actions that were taken against an alert.
• The Result Summary Report displays a summary of the search service results that were returned in
the alert.
• The FraudPoint Score Report displays the FraudPoint Score results that were returned by the service.
• The InstantID Report displays the InstantID results that were returned by the service.
• The Screening List Report provides information about screening list matches that are returned in the
alert.

Alert Reports in the New Alert View
XG lets users generate certain reports when they view an alert in the new alert view.
The following reports are available depending on the data in the alerts:
• The List Screening Report provides the screening list results for the alert. You can choose if the report
includes only the displayed columns or all the available columns for the field sets.
• The OFAC Report can be used to report when you determine that an input entity is a true match to an
entity on an OFAC screening list.
• The Record History Report lists the events and actions that were taken against an alert.
• The Alert View Report lists the sections of the alert that is currently viewed in the new alert view.
These sections include results, record details, and record history. You choose whether to expand the
sections to display the section content. For list screening results, you can also choose whether to
expand the full profiles to display the match details.
• The Result Summary Report displays a summary of the search service results that were returned in
the alert.

Alert List Report
The Alert List report contains the alerts that were returned in the query. For each alert, the report lists
the entity name, the ID type and number, the InstantID index, the number of matches, the account ID,
the alert status, the origin of the alert, and the date that the alert was created.
The report is available as a PDF file. The report is available only when multiple alerts are selected in an
alert list.

results, record details, and record history. You choose whether to expand the sections to display the
section content. For list screening results, you can also choose whether to expand the full profiles to
display the match details.
The report is available as a PDF file. This report is not available in the classic alert view.

summary for each alert created from the search.
This report is available only when you view a list of payment transaction alerts or when you view a
payment transaction alert in the classic alert view. This report is available in the following file types: PDF
or CSV.

OFAC Report
You can create an OFAC report within XG when you determine an input entity is a true match to an entity
on an OFAC screening list.
You can create an OFAC Report of Blocked Transactions or an OFAC Report of Rejected Transactions. You
can download the report as a PDF file to submit to OFAC.
You can only create an OFAC report for an alert that contains a match against an OFAC list. If you want
your organization's information to be populated on the OFAC report, then you must first enter that
information on the Organization page. When you generate an OFAC report, XG saves the OFAC report
information with the alert and adds an OFAC Report Created event to the record history.
This report is available as a PDF file.

Screening List Report
The Screening List Report provides information about the screening list matches that are returned in the
alert.
This report is available only when you view an alert list or when you view an alert in the classic view. The
file is available as a PDF file.
The report may include the following information:
Search Input
The report provides an overview of the input entity information that was searched.
Alert Information
The report provides the following alert information: alert status, alert assignment, and alert state.
This information is not provided for real-time searches that did not report a match.
Match Information
The report provides the match information for each reported match in the alert. This information is
not provided if the search did not report a match.
Input Information
The report provides the input information. This information includes the entity type and the
predefined search that was used. This information is provided only if the search did not report a
match.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 114

CONFIDENTIAL

When the option is configured in the predefined search, the report provides match indicator information
when the ACH (Automated Clearing House) input information contains an indicator that a third-party
screener reported an OFAC match on the input entity. This information is provided only for ACH input
records.
When the option is configured in the predefined search, the report may provide a true match update
when the screening list information is different from what is contained in the corresponding True Match
accept list record.
When the option is configured in the predefined search, the report may provide a false match update
when new entity information is found.
