Chapter 5

Ba t ch Sea rches
Batch searches let you search multiple records in a single run by uploading a file for processing.
You can manually upload files one at a time through the LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) application.
You can also use the Automatic Batch feature and third-party tools to upload multiple files or larger files
to the watched folders for processing.
If an accept list that is included in the predefined search is updated while a batch file is
processing, then XG uses the updated accept list to search the batch records as soon as the
updated accept list is available.
Related Information
Predefined Searches on page 251

Supported Input Files
XG supports input files that contain standard parsed data, payment transaction data, or unparsed data.
You can search files that contain standard parsed data that is provided in separate, clearlydefined fields. The length limitation for file names is 50 characters. The following file types are
supported: .txt, .csv, .ach, .xml, and .dat. The files must be encoded using ASCII, Unicode, or UTF-8. The
files can be in a delimited format or in a fixed format. You create batch formats to define the entity
information in the file.
The parsed files can contain column headings in the first row to help identify the type of data that is
contained in each column. For optimal searching, the file should contain only individual records or only
business records. All dates in the file must be in the same format.
You can also search payment transaction files. You use the following XG default formats to identify the
entity information:
•
•
•
•

XG - ACH
XG - Fedwire
XG - ISO 20022
XG - SWIFT

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 116

CONFIDENTIAL

In addition, you can use the XG - Unstructured default format to process files that are not parsed. The
product searches the files one text string at a time. This type of searching yields different results than
searching a file with parsed fields.
Related Information
Batch Formats on page 134
Supported Batch Files on page 137

Input Fields for Batch Searches
You determine what information is included in the files for batch processing. The product works best
with files in which the entity information is structured consistently in defined fields.
At a minimum, a batch record must contain a first name and a last name, or the record must contain
a full name. The additional information that you can provide depends on the type of entities that the
file contains. Batch files can contain data for one of the following entity types: business, individual,
unknown, or text entities. An unknown entity can be a business or an individual. A text entity is one text
field of unstructured data and an optional ID.
®

LexisNexis Risk Solutions recommends that you resolve issues of missing and corrupt data within
your files before you perform batch searches for optimal processing.
Related Information
Account Information Fields on page 117
Additional Information Fields on page 118
Name and Gender Fields on page 119
ID Fields on page 120
Address and Location Fields on page 128
Phone Fields on page 130

A c co un t I nf orm atio n Fields
The input fields that are available vary for real-time searches, batch searches, or custom screening list
records. The entity type also affects the available fields.
The following table list the fields alphabetically and indicates when the field is available by purpose and
entity type.
Table legend:
• I = Individual
• B = Business

• T = Text
• U = Unknown

• V = Vessel
• C = Country

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 117

A d di t i o n al I nfo rmat ion Fields
The input fields that are available vary for real-time searches, batch searches, or custom screening list
records. The entity type also affects the available fields.
The following table lists the fields alphabetically and indicates when the field is available by purpose and
entity type.
Table legend:
• I = Individual
• B = Business

• T = Text
• U = Unknown

• V = Vessel
• C = Country

When single records are directly added to custom screening lists, additional Comments fields are
available for various data elements.
For certain IDs, fields other than the Number field are not applicable due to the nature of the ID. These
fields are available only for single records that are directly added to custom screening lists.
The Date of Birth field and the Citizenship fields are displayed with identifications for real-time
searches.

Related Information
Account Information Fields on page 117

A d dr e s s an d Loc ation Fields
The input fields that are available vary for real-time searches, batch searches, or custom screening list
records. The entity type also affects the available fields.
The following table lists the fields alphabetically and indicates when the field is available by purpose and
entity type.
Table legend:
• I = Individual
• B = Business

• T = Text
• U = Unknown

• V = Vessel
• C = Country

When single records are directly added to custom screening lists, additional Comments fields are
available for various data elements.
For certain IDs, fields other than the Number field are not applicable due to the nature of the ID. These
fields are available only for single records that are directly added to custom screening lists.
The following fields are not available for parsed addresses in batch files: Address Line 1 and
Address Line 2. The following fields are available only for parsed addresses in batch files: Building
Number, Street Name, Street Number, Street Type, and Sub Building Number.

Additional Record Entities
Certain data strings indicate that an additional entity may be present in the address.
The following data strings are commonly found in the batch file records:
•
•
•
•
•

ATTENTION
ATTN
ATTN:
ATT:
ATT (with trailing or surrounding spaces)

•
•
•
•
•

C/O
CARE OF
DBA (doing business as)
FBO
%

If the product finds one of these data strings in a record, then the product searches the data that follows
the string using the selected screening list and the current search settings. If the product finds a match
for the data that follows the string, then an open alert is generated that includes the searched entity and
the entity in the data string.

CONFIDENTIAL

Manual File Uploads
XG lets you manually upload a batch file through the XG user interface. You can only manually upload
files that are less than the file size maximum for your XG system. For larger files, you can use the
Automatic Batch feature to transfer files directly to the XG server.
When you perform a batch search, you must specify the following information:
•
•
•
•
•

The batch file to process
The batch file format
The division access
The predefined search
If applicable, the GLBA (Gramm-Leach-Bliley Act) Permissible Use choice and the DPPA (Driver’s
Privacy Protection Act) Permissible Use choice
• The alert distribution method
• The email notifications

Upload a File
You can manually upload a file through the XG application for batch searching.
To view a training video about this task, see the training that is available on the LexisNexis® Risk
Solutions Customer Support at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Batch, and click Upload File.

2.

Select the file that you want to upload.

3.

Click Add Format, or click an existing format that you want to edit.

4.

Select the division of users who can access the alerts that are generated from the search.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 132

CONFIDENTIAL

5.

Select the predefined search.
Predefined searches are available for a search only when they meet the following criteria:
• The entity type of the input data is supported by the selected search services.
For example, input records with an unknown entity type cannot be searched by certain search
services.
• The input data meets the requirements of the selected search services.
For example, input records with only a full name cannot be searched by certain search services.
• The user has access to the predefined search based on division access and role access.

6.

Depending on the search services that are selected in the predefined search, select a GLBA
permissible use.

7.

Depending on the search services that are selected in the predefined search, select a DPPA
permissible use.

8.

Preview the file to confirm that the format correctly represents the file structure. If the format does
not correctly represent the fields in the file, then edit the file or edit the format to make them
match, and the file.
To prevent errors, consider all potential files that might be processed with the batch format
before making any changes.
XG previews and validates the format of the first 100KB in standard files or the format of payment
transaction files that are less than 100KB. This validation helps ensure that the file processes
successfully. If the file and the format do not match, then the product may return inaccurate
results.

9.

Determine which users are assigned to the alerts that are generated from the search:
• To assign alerts to a role and let any user in the selected roles and division process the alerts,
click Roles, and select the role.
Only the roles that are assigned to users who are associated with the selected division are
available for selection.
• To assign alerts to specific users in a round-robin order, click Users, and select the users.
Only the users who belong to the selected division are listed.

10. Set up batch email notifications.
Possible options:
• None
No batch email notification is sent.
• Only when the batch generates alerts
A batch email notification is sent only when the batch search generates an alert.
• When the batch is complete
A batch email notification is sent when the batch search is complete, whether or not alerts are
generated.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 133

CONFIDENTIAL

The default email message displays the file name, the server name, the beginning and ending time
of the file search, the number of records processed, and the number of open alerts and errors.
11. To include the details about the alerts in batch email notifications, select Include Transaction
Details.
This option is only available when a payment transaction format is selected and an email
notification is selected.
12. Click Start Batch.
Result:

Files are deleted from the system after processing is complete. If a batch upload stalls for two hours or
more, then the product deletes the batch upload.
Do not navigate from the page before the upload is complete or your upload may not successfully
complete.
If you assign the alert to a user, then the user settings may set XG to send an email notification to the
assigned user.
If you assign the alert to a role, then the role settings may set XG to send an email notification to the
users in the assigned role. Only users who belong to the division that can access the alert receive an
email notification.
After you complete this task:

You can manage the batch search as a batch run.

Roles on page 225
Divisions on page 240

Batch Formats
You create batch formats to define the structure of the fields in the files that you want to search.
Batch formats help the product correctly compare similar information during searches. For example,
a batch format helps the product compare the first names in your batch file to the first names in a
screening list.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 134

CONFIDENTIAL

In Microsoft Internet Explorer, performance may be affected when you map files that contain
more than 1,000 columns or that contain records with more than 30 entities. If you frequently
search these types of batch files, then consider using Google Chrome as your web browser
instead.
Related Information
Delete a Batch Format on page 142

File Format Planning
Files may be formatted in various ways. You must determine the format of the file so that you can
create a format in the product. You may need assistance from your IT personnel to determine certain
information (for example, encoding).
Before you create any type of format, you must know the following information about the file:
• What type of records are in the file (for example, individuals or businesses)?
• Does the file contain multiple entities per record?
• How are the dates formatted?
The dates that are in the file and that you want to include in the record must be in the same
format.
• Does the file contain column headings in the first row?
The column headings in the file do not have to exactly match an XG field name. For example, a Street
Address column in a file can correspond to an Address Line 1 field in the product.
• What is the file encoding method (ASCII, Unicode, or UTF-8)?
Most files are encoded in ASCII and are easy to read using a text editor (for example, Notepad).
• Do you need to set a default country that the product adds to empty Country fields?
• Is the address line information parsed into separate address fields?
For example, the address line has separate fields for house number and for street name.
• Which data elements from your file do you want to include in a record?
A file can contain elements that you do not want to include in a format. For example, a file may
contain account lead information that you do not need for searches.
• Is the file in a delimited format or a fixed format?
Before you create a delimited format, you must also know the following information about the file:
• What type of delimiter is used (for example, tab or comma)?
• Does the file contain double plain quotes as a second type of delimiter?
• What is the order of the data elements?

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 135

CONFIDENTIAL

Before you create a fixed format, you should also know the following information about the file:
• What is the total record length, which includes ending characters?
• Does each record end with a return or a line feed?
• What is the length of each column and the position of the first character in the column?
Related Information
Multiple Entities per Record on page 136
Supported Batch Files on page 137
Delete a Batch Format on page 142
Set Up a Delimited Batch Format on page 138
Set Up a Fixed Batch Format on page 140

Multiple Entities per Record
XG can process files that contain up to 30 entities per record.
For example, a file from a financial institution may contain multiple account holders for each record.
These records contain multiple columns of name information, such as First Name1, Last Name1, First
Name2, and Last Name2. In the format, you indicate which columns are associated with each entity.
Multiple Entities File Example

1 = Entity 1
2 = Entity 2
3 = Information that is associated with both entities

Supported Batch Files
XG can search files that use ASCII, Unicode, or UTF-8 encoding. The files can be in either a delimited or
fixed format.
The files can contain column headings in the first row to help identify the type of data that is contained
in each column. For optimal searching, the file should contain only individual records or only business
records.
All dates in the file must be in the same format.
Related Information
File Format Planning on page 135
Multiple Entities per Record on page 136

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 137

CONFIDENTIAL

De li m i t e d Fil es
The files in a delimited format contain records that end with a carriage-return character and that vary in
size according to the length of the data in each field. These files use special characters to indicate where
each field ends.
When you view a delimited file in a basic text editor (for example, Notepad), the fields typically do not
line up with their column headings.
To prevent the product from separating the data incorrectly, designate a delimiter character that
is not found in the data portion of the file. For example, you should typically avoid using commas
as field delimiters because commas are common in full addresses.
Semicolon-Delimited File Example

Set Up a Delimited Batch Format
You must set up a batch format to tell XG how to read and parse your input file.
To view a training video about this task, see the training that is available on the Customer Support at
https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Batch, and click Batch Formats.

2.

Click Add Format, or select an existing format that you want to edit.
To prevent errors, consider all potential files that might be processed with the batch format
before making any changes.
XG previews and validates the format of the first 100KB in standard files or the format of payment
transaction files that are less than 100KB. This validation helps ensure that the file processes
successfully. If the file and the format do not match, then the product may return inaccurate
results.

3.

To use an input file as a structure template, select the file in the Example File section.
The product displays the example file in the Field Mapping section.

4.

Enter a unique format name.

5.

To populate the settings from an existing format, select Use a saved format, and select a format.
This option is not available if you edit an existing format.

6.

Select Delimited as the format type.

7.

Select the character that separates each field as the field delimiter.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 138

CONFIDENTIAL

8.

To set the product to read double quotes as delimiter characters, select Read double quotes (") as
delimiters.

9.

Select the entity type.

10. Select the date format.
In place of slashes, the product also accepts dashes (-), periods (.), or spaces.
11. If the first row is a column header, then select Read the first line as a column header.
If you select an example file, then the product displays the column heading names in the Field
Mapping section. The product does not search the first row.
12. Select the encoding type.
13. To add a country to empty Country fields, select a country.
If at least one address field is mapped in the batch format, then this option populates empty
Country fields with the default country.
This option is useful for the country rule for automatic false positives.
14. If the address line information in your input file is separated into multiple fields, then select Parsed
address fields.
Parsed address fields are displayed in the column menus in the Field Mapping section.
15. If the file contains multiple entities per record, then select Allow multiple entities.
The Add Entity button is displayed in the Field Mapping section.
16. If you used an example file, for each column that you want to search, select the field in the column
menu that corresponds to the column contents.
If you do not want to search the column, then make sure (none) is selected for the column.
17. If you did not use an example file, then map each field that you want to search:
a. Select the field in the column menu that corresponds to the first field in the file.
b. Map additional fields as necessary.
To add a column, click (Add new column). To remove a column, click
(Remove this
column). To change the column order, enter a number next to the column name.
18. If the file can contain multiple entities per record, then complete the following steps for each
additional entity:
a. Click Add Entity.
An Entity <#> button is displayed.
b. Map only the columns in the file that you want to search for the entity.
To make changes to another entity in the record, click the entity button for that entity.
19. Verify that the file data appears correctly in the Field Mapping section.
20. Click Save.
21. If you selected a default country, then click Yes to save the format.

F ix e d F i l e s
The files in a fixed format contain records that are the same length.
The width of each column is a predetermined number of characters. When you view a fixed-format file in
a basic text editor (for example, Notepad), the fields line up with their column headings.

Batch Run Management
Batch runs let you manage batch searches or alert imports and any associated alerts in one area.
You can complete the following tasks to manage a batch run:
• Determine whether batch processing is complete.
• Review the batch run details. For example, you can view the processing times and the number of
screening list matches that were generated from the search.
• Delete the batch run and associated alerts.
• Add notes to the batch run. For example, you can note the process actions and decisions.
• For batch runs for batch searches, reprocess records with errors. A (Run Recovery) icon displays for
batch runs with reported record errors.
• Generate a Batch Summary report (batch searches only) and a Batch Details report.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 142

CONFIDENTIAL

Review a Batch Run
You can review a batch run for each batch search or alert import that is processed. You can also add
notes to the batch run.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Batch, and click Batch Runs.

2.

Select the date range in which the file was searched or imported from the date list in the upperright corner of the page.

3.

Select a run type.

4.

Click the batch file or the alert import file.
The product page indicates the processing status of the file. The status is only for the records that
have been processed at that point. Refresh your browser to view the updated results.
Click the hyperlinks to view any errors or alerts.

5.

Review the details of the batch run.
To find alerts with errors, use the Errors query options. For example, you can find alerts with
search service errors to reorder certain searches.

6.

To view the alerts that were generated from the batch search, click the alert count value, and click
Leave.

7.

To view the alerts that returned errors, click the error count value, and click Leave.

8.

To add notes to a batch run, expand the Notes section, enter the note, and click Add Note.
You cannot delete batch run notes.

9.

For batch files, to view the predefined search settings that were used to perform the search, expand
the Predefined Search section and additional subsections.

Reprocess Records with Errors
For batch runs for batch searches, you can reprocess records that returned search service errors.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Batch, and click Batch Runs.

2.

Select the date range in which the file was searched from the date list in the upper-right corner of
the page.

3.

Select Batch as the run type.

4.

Find the file to reprocess.
The batch searches that did not complete and need to be resubmitted display a run error as the
status. You cannot reprocess records for these files.

5.

Click (Run Recovery) next to the file.
A note is added to the batch run. A Run Recovery event is listed in the record history of the alert
that is generated from each record that is reprocessed.

Delete a Batch Run
You can delete a batch run that is no longer applicable to your review processes. The system deletes
batch runs one at a time. You cannot simultaneously delete multiple batch runs.
When you delete a batch run, you also delete the alerts that were generated from the batch search or
imported into the database. Consider exporting the alerts before you delete the batch run. Alternatively,
you can delete the alerts rather than deleting the batch run. This option decreases the size of your
product database, but retains a record that the file was searched or imported. You can also add a note to
the batch run to indicate that you deleted the alerts.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Batch, and click Batch Runs.

2.

Select the date range in which the file was searched or imported from the date list in the upperright corner of the page.

3.

Select a run type.

4.

Click

5.

Click Yes.

(Delete) next to the batch run.

Batch Summary Report
The Batch Summary report contains a summary for each file that was processed and included in the
report. A report can only be generated for batch runs for batch searches. A report cannot be generated
for batch runs for imported alerts.
The summary includes the search date and time, the user name of the user who processed the file, the
division that can access the results of the file, the name of the file, the predefined search that was used
to process the file, and a summary of the results.
If a batch run is still processing, then the report displays the results for only records that have
been processed. The product page indicates the processing status of each file.

Automatic Batch Searches
The Automatic Batch feature provides a secure means for you to transfer large files to the XG server for
processing. This feature lets you automate batch file processing with the help of third-party products.
With third-party file creation and transfer tools, you can schedule file transfers to server folders. The
product processes the files according to the Automatic Batch configuration that is associated with the
folder.

SFTP Client and Encryption
XG Service clients are required to use PGP (Pretty Good Privacy) encryption and SFTP (secure file transfer
protocol) to securely transfer files across networks. XG Enterprise clients who complete Automatic Batch
processing within their fire walls may not need this file security.
Gpg4win (GNU Privacy Guard for Windows) is free and open-source PGP software. Gpg4win is available
to download at https://gpg4win.org/. Other PGP software may also be compatible.
SFTP is a protocol that encrypts both commands and data. SSH2 (Secure Shell 2) is a protocol that offers
authentication, encryption, and data integrity during file transfers. This third-party software provides a
double layer of file protection during transfer by securing the data contained in the files as well as the
communication route.
LexisNexis Risk Solutions provides XG Service users with the IP address, the client upload directory
credentials, and the client output directory credentials that they need to access the SFTP server.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 146

CONFIDENTIAL

VanDyke Software's SecureFX includes SFTP and SSH2 communications. SecureFX has been tested with
XG; however, other SFTP client products may also be compatible. For more information, see http://
www.vandyke.com.
Customer Support does not provide support for third-party products.

B a tc h F i le E ncryp tion Keys
If you use PGP encryption, then you must download and import the XG public key into your PGP
encryption software. You use this key to encrypt the files that you transfer to the SFTP server.
LexisNexis Risk Solutions notifies XG Service customers when the XG public key changes. When a new key
is available, you delete the existing public key in your PGP encryption software and download and import
the new public key.
If you encrypt a file with an expired XG public key, then the product cannot decrypt the file and reports
an error.

Duplicate Matches
If searches are performed simultaneously or before alert processing is completed for previous searches,
then XG may generate duplicate matches. You can configure the product to not generate a duplicate
match from batch searches when an open alert already contains an identical match.
To suppress a duplicate match, the following conditions must be met:
• The input information is in a standard structured format. The input information cannot be an
unstructured record or a payment transaction (EFT (electronic funds transfer)) record.
• The list match in the two alerts must be identical.
• The input information in the two alerts must be identical (for example, uppercase/lowercase or date
formats).
• The existing alert must be current (not archived) with an open alert state.
You can additionally set the product to not generate the duplicate match only when the alert can be
accessed by the same division.
This feature does not suppress duplicate matches from real-time searches. The feature also does not
suppress matches that contain errors.
When this feature is configured, alerts that contain the following validation message are
suppressed: The name is empty or contains invalid data.

Configure Duplicate Match Settings
Duplicate match settings in the application affect subsequent list matches that are generated in batch
searches.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Batch, and click Duplicate Matches.

2.

To suppress duplicate matches, click Don't generate duplicate list screening matches for batch
searches.

S c r e en i ng Lists
You can use the following types of lists in the list screening service: screening lists that your organization
subscribes to, accept lists, the White List, and custom screening lists.

Available Screening Lists
Your organization subscribes to screening lists that are provided by LexisNexis® Risk Solutions and makes
them available to your LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) client instance for the list screening service.
You can view any new screening lists after they are made available to the client instance and after the
lists are updated.
The following information is displayed for each list:
• The Type column displays Entities if the list contains individual records, business records, or vessel
records. The column displays Countries if the list contains country records.
• The Source Date column displays the date and the time that the source agency last updated its data.
• The LexisNexis Date column displays the date and the time that LexisNexis Risk Solutions updated the
list.
In XG Service, LexisNexis Risk Solutions updates the screening lists that your organization subscribes to.
In XG Enterprise, your organization updates these screening lists in Enterprise Manager.

Accept Lists
Accept lists can help your organization manage false positive matches and monitor data changes to true
matches.

False Positives
You can use accept lists to reduce the number of times the same false positive matches must be
re-processed. After you determine that a match is a false positive, you can add the match to an accept
list. When the accept list is included in a predefined search that is used for future searches, XG uses the
match information to suppress the same match in future searches.
XG can be set to generate an alert that contains a false match update when new match information is
found for certain data elements that are in an accept list record. You can also set the default settings
that are used for all predefined searches. You can select the following data elements to generate a false
match update:
•
•
•
•

Address
AKA (also known as)
DOB (date of birth)
Citizenship

•
•
•
•

Gender
ID Numbers
Name
Phone

False match updates are designed to alert you to new match information that may need further
investigation to determine whether the record should remain on the accept list as a false positive. For
example, if you previously added a match to an accept list that did not contain a matching DOB, and then
XG found a matching DOB in a later search, XG would generate a false match update.

True Match Updates
You can also use accept lists to monitor data changes to specific profiles.
XG can be set to generate an alert that contains a true match update when list entity information
changes for a true match in an accept list record.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 159

CONFIDENTIAL

To help reduce internal risk, carefully assess which users have list privileges.
Accept List Processing

At a high-level, accept list processing involves the following stages:
1.
2.
3.
4.

A list screening search is performed.
The alert is reviewed and added to an accept list.
The predefined search is configured to use the accept list.
In repeated searches, the accept list suppresses the same alert.

Related Information
Accept List Management on page 163
Accept List Record Management on page 166
Accept List Report on page 170

What Are False Positives?
False positives occur when the input information that you searched is similar enough to screening list
information to generate a match, but you determine that the search subject is not the entity listed on
the screening list.
XG uses sophisticated logic to help eliminate the most apparent false positive matches. You can also use
the Automatic False Positive rules in predefined searches to help determine whether a potential match is
a false positive.
Related Information
Rules for Automatic False Positives on page 263

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 160

CONFIDENTIAL

Accept Lists in Process
Accept lists help reduce the number of recurring matches that your organization must manually review
by letting users add alerts to a list to prevent the same alerts from being reported in future searches.
You add an alert that you have investigated to an accept list based on your review process. The
accept list record contains the input information that your organization provided for the search and the
screening list information for each match in the alert.
In addition to the entity name, screening list records can contain multiple AKA names. XG determines
which name in the screening list record best matches the name in the input record. This “best matching
name” and the entity name in the screening list record are added to each match in the accept list record.
The best matching name and the entity name in the screening list record may be the same.
Accept list records do not store MR (machine readable) Line 1 and Line 2 information that is
provided in the input information for passports or visas.
Each match in the accept list record can also contain the information that is needed for false match
updates. When the information is available in a new search, XG adds the following information to an
accept list match:
•
•
•
•
•
•

Entity unique ID
File date
Published date
Match state
Match date
Best DOB

You add the accept list to your predefined search. XG compares the input entity to the accept list entities
to determine if an alert should be generated. If the product can suppress all screening list matches, then
the alert is not generated.
Related Information
Set up Predefined Searches on page 252
Apply an Alert Decision to a Single Record on page 90
Apply an Alert Decision to Selected Records on page 92
Alert Decision Setup on page 293

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 161

CONFIDENTIAL

Required Input Entity Information
The alert must contain specific input entity information before you can add the record to an accept list.
The alert must contain the following information:
• The input entity information must contain a name.
An alert may not contain an entity name if the input record was included in a batch file in which one
of the following cases is true:
• The batch file was large enough during upload to prevent missing name errors in the preview
validation from not allowing the search.
• The batch file was processed using the XG - Unstructured format.
• The batch file was processed using a payment transaction format, and the match was generated
from the text string context.
• The input record must contain a unique identifier.
The accept lists use these unique identifiers to find the matching accept list records.
Unique identifiers can be an ID number (with the exception of group ID or provider ID) or a complete
address.
If an ID number was not provided in the search, then you can add an account ID in the record
details of the alert and add the alert to an accept list. You should not provide non-unique ID numbers
because this type of data can adversely affect accept list processing.
The complete address can be made up of at least four words or numbers in the following field
combinations:
• Address Line 1, City, and State
• Address Line 1 and Postal Code
• Address Line 1, City, and Country

Apply an Alert Decision to a Single Record on page 90
Apply an Alert Decision to Selected Records on page 92
Alert Decision Setup on page 293

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 162

CONFIDENTIAL

Accept List Management
You can use multiple accept lists to serve different business units or processing needs.
For example, text records or payment transaction records are structured differently than the records that
are contained in a typical batch file. Therefore, consider using a separate list for text records or payment
transaction records. You can also create an accept list for a general license that is applicable to your
business. If the general license is ever revoked, then you can simply remove the list for that general
license from your predefined search.
Large lists can affect system performance. To help avoid issues, you can set up multiple accept lists
to reduce the size of a large list.
For each list, you can perform the following management tasks: set up, delete, import, and export.
When you set up an accept list, you can set the following options:
•
•
•
•

Set the divisions that are allowed to access the list.
Require users to select an alert status when they add an alert to the list.
Treat account numbers as unique identifiers.
In XG Enterprise, make the list available to share with other XG client instances. You share the list in
Enterprise Manager.

Lists that are exported from XG can be imported into the same version of the product. You can export an
accept list into an XML-formatted file. For example, you may want to export a list so that you can view
the data using third-party software such as Microsoft Excel. Alternatively, you may want to export a list
to retain a copy for your audit records before you permanently delete the list from XG.
If you want to integrate the data into third-party products, then you can use
theAccept List Export XSD to validate the data structure. You can access the XSD (XML Schema
Definition) from the related article on the LexisNexis® Risk Solutions Customer Support at https://
lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/.
Customer Support does not assist with processes that you perform on exported files.

Set Up an Accept List
You must set up an accept list before users can add alerts to the list as part of their processing.
To view a training video about this task, see the training that is available on the Customer Support at
https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to List Management, and click Accept Lists.

2.

Click Add List, or click an existing list that you want to edit.

3.

Enter a unique name and a description.
XG Enterprise users who create shared lists should consider whether to use a naming convention
that easily identifies the list as being available to other XG client instances. For example, add an (S)
or $ to the end of the name.

4.

To require a user to select a status when the user adds an alert to this list, select Require the user
to set a status when an alert is added to an accept list.

5.

To generate alerts for entities where multiple data elements match, but the account numbers are
different, select Treat account numbers as unique identifiers on search.

6.

To share lists with other client instances in XG Enterprise, select Make available enterprise-wide.
This option is available only when you create a list. Only users in the client instance in which the list
was created can add records to the list or make other list edits. Users in other client instances can
include the list in a predefined search.

7.

Enter any comments.

8.

Select the divisions of users that can access the list.
This option is not available if only one division exists for the client instance. Only divisions that you
have access to are displayed. You cannot remove divisions that you do not have access to.

9.

Click Save.
You must add records to the list or import records into the list before you can include the list in a
predefined search.

After you complete this task:

To help prevent false positive matches, you must include the list in relevant predefined searches.
XG Enterprise users must enable access to the shared lists in Enterprise Manager before they can
be included in a predefined search. For more information about sharing lists, see the LexisNexis®
Bridger Insight® XG Enterprise Manager Help.

Query the List to Find Records
You search, or query, a list to find records that meet selected criteria.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to List Management, and click Accept Lists.

2.

Access the Query page by completing one of the following tasks:
• Click (Query) next to the list that you want to query.
• Click the list that you want to query, and click New Query.

3.

Select an entity type to query.
Possible values:
• Any
• Individual
• Business
• Unkonwn
The available fields change depending on the entity type that you select.

4.

Select or enter the query criteria.
To be considered a match, the record information must match all selected criteria. If you want your
search to return all the records in the list, then do not select or enter any criteria.
You can enter an asterisk (*) in a field to return the records that meet your criteria and that contain
any data in the field where you put the asterisk.
If you want your search to return only records that are set as true matches, then select Return only
records with True Match dispositioning. If you want your search to exclude any records that are set
as true matches, then select Exclude records with True Match dispositioning.

5.

Click Find.

White List
The White List is designed to prevent recurring false positives that are found from unparsed data that
cannot be added to the accept lists.
The White List helps you automatically process recurring false positives with Automatic False Positive
rules that are based on the name matches that were reported in previous searches. This feature uses
word-for-word matching between the input name or the input context and the entity name or the AKA
name in a screening list record.
For example, the payment transaction records that you search using the default file format contain
unparsed data that is not contained in defined fields. Even more specifically, the White List works well
for cases in which you are sure that the input name and the match name are not the same entity. For
example, “Libya Bank” (a business) matches “Libya” (a country).
The use of the White List affects how the list screening service finds and processes matches.
LexisNexis Risk Solutions recommends that you thoroughly test the White List and use this feature
with caution.
At a high-level, you add the input name or input context (text strings from unparsed records) that
matches a screening list record to a White List record. You also add the entity names that are contained
on the screening list that your input entity matches. In future searches, the list screening service applies
the Automatic False Positive rules to the input records that match the White List records.
The White List feature is a less sophisticated method for managing false positives than the Accept List
feature. The accept lists use more data elements to reduce false positives. These data elements include
names, addresses, IDs, and other information. Whenever possible, use the more powerful Accept List
feature to better manage false positives.
The White List can contain a maximum of 1,000 records.
White List entries offer options to help you specify the conditions in which the list screening service
suppresses alerts. For example, you can provide the following information to specify which input
information (record text) the list screening service acts on:
• Use an asterisk (*) as a wild card to represent zero to multiple characters in a text pattern.
• Provide a regex (regular expression) to match a text pattern.
• Provide input ID types and values.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 171

CONFIDENTIAL

You can also provide information about the list entries (match text) that the list screening service acts
on:
• Provide the specific screening lists.
• Provide the specific source record numbers of the list entries.
• Set the minimum value and the maximum value (70–100) for the match confidence score.
White List Processing

At a high level, White List processing involves the following stages:
1.
2.
3.
4.

A list screening search is performed.
The alert is reviewed, and a match is added as a White List entry.
The predefined search is configured to use the White List.
In repeated searches, the Automatic False Positive rules are applied to the same match.

White List in Process
The White List compares input information to White List records to identify false positives.
You determine that a name match is a false positive. You create a White List record that contains the
name match to use the Automatic False Positive rules to process the match in future searches.
Each White List record contains the input name or input context that you determined was a false positive
as “record text.” Input context is the text string in unparsed data that generated the match. In the White
List record, the record text must be unique, or the record text must contain a unique identifier.
In the White List record, you add the entity names that are on the screening lists that match against the
record text as “match text” entries. Each match text must be unique, or the match text must contain
a unique screening list or a unique record identifier. For each match text, you can set the following
requirements that a match must include:
• The screening list that contains the match text.
• The record number of the screening list record that contains the match text.
The record number is the profile ID (the Number field in classic alert view) in the alert match details.
• The match confidence score range (70-100) that a match must meet.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 172

CONFIDENTIAL

If a record text matches the same name on multiple screening lists, then you add only one match text
entry. For example, you search “Zachary Thul,” and the data matches the following records:
• Zachary Thule on List A
• Zach Thul on List B
• Zachary Thule on List C
On the White List, you enter “Zachary Thul” as the record text and “Zachary Thule” and “Zach Thul” as
two match texts. You do not repeat “Zachary Thule” as a third match text.
You configure the White List in a predefined search. The list screening service applies the Automatic
False Positive rules to the matches that are generated in future searches when the following situations
occur:
• The record text entry of a White List record matches the input name or the input context.
• The match text entries of the same White List record exactly match the entity names on the screening
lists. The match text entries also must meet any specified requirements for the screening lists, the
record number, or the entity score range.
The Automatic False Positive rules can cause the list screening service to perform the following actions:
• Do not create an alert.
• Create an alert with a closed alert state and no alert status.
• Create an alert with an open alert state and an Automatic False Positive alert status.
To be a White List match, the record text must be an exact match to the match text unless you provide
a wild card or a regular expression. You can use an asterisk (*) as a wild card to replace a character
anywhere in the record text. Use one asterisk for each character that you want to replace. To match on
both Smith and Smyth, for example, you can provide sm*th as the record text entry.
You can also use a regular expression to find matches on text that meet a set pattern.
The Regular Expression option may affect the alerts that are returned. This option requires a
good understanding of regular expressions. Thoroughly test the regular expressions that you
provide. Customer Support does not assist with creating regular expressions.
For more information about regular expressions, you can refer to the following third-party sources or
other third-party sources:
• http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/az24scfc.aspx
• http://www.regular-expressions.info/tutorial.html
Related Information
White List on page 171

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 173

CONFIDENTIAL

Set Up White List Records
You can create or edit White List records.
Procedure:

a. To add an entry, click Add Entry.

matches your input name.
c. To limit matches to a particular screening list, select the list.
d. To limit matches to a particular record, enter the record number.
You can find the record number in the Number field of the alert match details.
e. To limit matches to a particular range for the match confidence score, enter the minimum score
and the maximum score.
f. To delete a match text entry, click

Custom Screening Lists
You can create your own lists to search your input data for purposes that are unique to your
organization. You add the custom screening lists to predefined searches and use them to report potential
matches.
For example, you might set up a list for each of the following reasons:
• To screen businesses and individuals against the FinCEN (Financial Crimes Enforcement Network)
314a list
• To record businesses or individuals who have committed fraud against your organization
• To screen individuals for compliance to Regulation O of the Federal Reserve
You can complete tasks to manage a whole list and you can complete tasks to manage records in a list.
To help reduce internal risk, carefully assess which users have privileges to use custom screening
lists.
You can use the Custom Screening List Report to manage your custom screening lists.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 175

CONFIDENTIAL

Input Fields for Custom Screening Lists
You determine the information that your custom screening lists contain. The product works best when
your screening list is structured consistently in defined fields.
At a minimum, a record must contain either information in the First Name field and the Last Name
field or information in the Full Name field. The additional information that you can provide depends on
the type of entities that the list contains. A list can contain data for one of the following entity types:
individual, business, vessel, or country.
LexisNexis Risk Solutions recommends that you clean up the custom screening lists before you
import them. Files with missing or corrupt data can generate errors. Files with unclean data can
cause you to spend time troubleshooting and can create file processing delays.
If the list is set up to use unique record IDs, then the format must contain a mapped field with the
same selected ID type. Every record in the import file must contain a unique ID with the selected
ID type.

Phone Fields on page 190

ID Fields
The input fields that are available vary for real-time searches, batch searches, or custom screening list
records. The entity type also affects the available fields.
The following table lists the fields alphabetically and indicates when the field is available by purpose and
entity type.
Table legend:
• I = Individual
• B = Business

• T = Text
• U = Unknown

• V = Vessel
• C = Country

When single records are directly added to custom screening lists, additional Comments fields are
available for various data elements.
For certain IDs, fields other than the Number field are not applicable due to the nature of the ID. These
fields are available only for single records that are directly added to custom screening lists.
The fields are grouped by ID type.

The input fields that are available vary for real-time searches, batch searches, or custom screening list
records. The entity type also affects the available fields.
The following table lists the fields alphabetically and indicates when the field is available by purpose and
entity type.
Table legend:
• I = Individual
• B = Business

• T = Text
• U = Unknown

• V = Vessel
• C = Country

When single records are directly added to custom screening lists, additional Comments fields are
available for various data elements.
For certain IDs, fields other than the Number field are not applicable due to the nature of the ID. These
fields are available only for single records that are directly added to custom screening lists.

The following fields are not available for parsed addresses in batch files: Address Line 1 and
Address Line 2. The following fields are available only for parsed addresses in batch files: Building
Number, Street Name, Street Number, Street Type, and Sub Building Number.

Custom Screening List Management
You can create country lists or an entity lists. Country lists contain the records of countries along with
their AKA names and locations. Entity lists contain the records of individuals, businesses, and vessels.
When you set up lists, you can set the following options:
•
•
•
•
•

Set the list to automatically index.
Set the list type to identify whether the list contains entities or countries.
For entity lists, set the ID type for the field that contains the entity unique ID.
Set the divisions that can access the list.
In XG Enterprise, make the list available to share with other client instances. You share the list in
Enterprise Manager. Only users in the client instance in which the list was created can add records
to the list or make other list edits. Users in other client instances can include the list in a predefined
search.

To manage custom screening lists, you can perform the following tasks:
• Import lists.
• Export lists.
• Index lists.
If you import or index large lists (more than one million records), then your system performance
may be affected. To help avoid issues, you can set up multiple lists to reduce the size of any one
list.

S e t U p a Cu st om Sc reening Li st
You can create or edit custom screening lists.
To view a training video about this task, see the training that is available on the Customer Support at
https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to List Management, and click Custom Screening Lists.

2.

Click Add List, or click an existing list that you want to edit.

3.

Enter a unique name and a description.
XG Enterprise users who create shared lists should consider whether to use a naming convention
that easily identifies the list as being available to other XG client instances. For example, add an (S)
or $ to the end of the name.

4.

To configure the list to index each time a change is made, select Automatically Index.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 192

CONFIDENTIAL

5.

Select a list type.
Possible values:
• Entity
• Country
This option is available only when you create a new list. The list type cannot be changed after the
list is created.

6.

To set the field that contains the entity unique ID for an entity list, complete the following steps:
a. Select Unique ID.
b. Select the ID type.
This option is available only when you create a new list. Every record in the list must contain a
unique ID with the selected ID type.

7.

To share lists with other client instances in XG Enterprise, select Make available enterprise-wide.
This option is available only when you create a list. Only users in the client instance in which the list

include the list in a predefined search.

8.

Enter any comments.

9.

Select the divisions of users that can access the list.
This option is not available if only one division exists for the client instance. Only divisions that you
have access to are displayed. You cannot remove divisions that you do not have access to.

10. Click Save.
You must add records to the list or import records into the list before you can include the list in a
predefined search.
After you complete this task:

XG Enterprise users must enable access to the shared lists in Enterprise Manager before they can
be included in a predefined search. For more information about sharing lists, see the LexisNexis®
Bridger Insight® XG Enterprise Manager Help.

C u s to m Screenin g List In dexin g
Indexing a list organizes the data to support faster and more accurate retrieval from the database.
You must index a list before you can search new or changed information. You can set up a list to
automatically index or manually index.
XG indexes the lists one at a time per server. When a list is configured to automatically index, XG indexes
the list when one of the following situations occur:
• One or more records are added to the list or deleted from the list.
• A record in the list was changed by a user.
• The setup options for the list were changed.
Lists that are set to automatically index are not indexed when the input information from alerts is added
to the list.
Small lists that change multiple times a day should be set to automatically index. Automatic
indexing helps ensure that changes to the lists are available for searching. For performance
reasons, manually index large lists that contain more than 50,000 records.
When you index a list, the following statuses identify the index status:
Pending
This status indicates that XG is set to build the list.
Processing
This status indicates that XG is building the list.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 194

CONFIDENTIAL

Built
This status indicates that XG has built the list and the list is waiting for deployment.
Loaded
This status indicates that XG uploaded the list and the list is ready for searches.
XG displays the last time that the list was indexed.
Related Information
Custom Screening List Record Management on page 204

Custom Screening List Formats
You create file formats to tell XG the structure of the data fields in custom screening lists.
File formats help XG place import file data into the appropriate record fields, or place export data from
a custom screening list into the appropriate fields of the export file. XG supports delimited formats and
fixed formats.
File Format Planning
The files that you import into custom screening lists may be formatted in different ways.
Before you create a file format to import the file, you should know the following information about the
file:
• What type of records are in the file (for example, individuals or businesses)?
• Are there multiple rows per record?
• What is the file encoding method (ASCII, Unicode, or UTF-8)?
Most files are encoded in ASCII and are easy to read using a text editor (for example, Notepad).
• Does the file contain column headings in the first row?
The column headings in the file do not have to exactly match an XG field name. For example, a Street
Address column in a file can correspond to an Address Line 1 field in the product.
• How are the dates formatted?
The dates that are in the file and that you want to include in the record must be in the same
format.
Before you create a delimited format, you must also know the following information about the file:
• What type of delimiter is used (for example, tab or comma)?
• Does the file contain double plain quotes as a second type of delimiter?
• What is the order of the data elements?
Before you create a fixed format, you should also know the following information about the file:
• What is the total record length, which includes ending characters?
• Does each record end with a return or a line feed?
• What is the length of each column and the position of the first character in the column?
Related Information
Multiple Rows per Record on page 197

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 196

CONFIDENTIAL

Multiple Rows per Record
The files that you want to import into custom screening lists can contain records with information that
spans multiple, consecutive rows. These files must contain a column that numbers each record. XG
considers rows with the same number to be part of the same record. The first record must be number 1,
and records must be numbered consecutively.
Information from the name fields that is provided in subsequent rows is not used in XG.
Multiple Row File Example

The following file example shows two records to import into a custom screening list. The first record
contains information in multiple rows. The second record contains information in a single row.

1 = Record
2 = Full Name
3 = Business Phone
4 = Address Line 1
5 = City
6 = State
7 = Postal Code

list.

Delimited Files
The files in a delimited format contain records that end with a carriage-return character and that vary in
size according to the length of the data in each field. These files use special characters to indicate where
each field ends.
When you view a delimited file in a basic text editor (for example, Notepad), the fields typically do not
line up with their column headings.
To prevent the product from separating the data incorrectly, designate a delimiter character that
is not found in the data portion of the file. For example, you should typically avoid using commas
as field delimiters because commas are common in full addresses.
Semicolon-Delimited File Example

Set Up a Delimited List Format
You can set up a list format for an import file that uses a delimiter to define the columns.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to List Management, and click Custom Screening Lists.

3.

Click Add Format, or select an existing format that you want to edit.
To prevent errors, consider all potential files that might be processed with the batch format
before making any changes.
XG previews and validates the format of the first 100KB in standard files or the format of payment
transaction files that are less than 100KB. This validation helps ensure that the file processes
successfully. If the file and the format do not match, then the product may return inaccurate
results.

delimiters.

11. Select the encoding type.

If you select an example file, then the product displays the column heading names in the Field
Mapping section. The product does not search the first row.

In place of slashes, the product also accepts dashes (-), periods (.), or spaces.

a. Select Multiple rows per record.

menu that corresponds to the column contents.
If you do not want to search the column, then make sure (none) is selected for the column. To add
a column, click (Add new column). To remove a column, click
(Remove this column).
16. If you did not use an example file, then map each field that you want to search:
a. Select the field in the column menu that corresponds to the first field in the file.
b. Map additional fields as necessary.

Fixed Files
The files in a fixed format contain records that are the same length.
The width of each column is a predetermined number of characters. When you view a fixed-format file in
a basic text editor (for example, Notepad), the fields line up with their column headings.
Fixed File Example

FinCEN Lists
FinCEN restricts access to its data. Your organization must obtain the data directly from FinCEN. You can
then import the FinCEN data into a custom screening list to scan as you would any other list.
Your organization is responsible for updating and managing the FinCEN data in XG.

S e t U p C us to m S creening Lists f or Fin CEN
You can import FinCEN data into a custom screening list to scan as you would any other list.
LexisNexis Risk Solutions previously recommended that you import the individual file and the business
file into one default custom screening list, FinCEN Individuals and Businesses, that is provided in
the product. LexisNexis Risk Solutions now recommends that you import the individual file and the
business file into separate lists that are created by your organization. If you currently use one list for both
files, then contact Customer Support before you begin using two lists, because changing your process
may cause accept list re-alerts.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 206

CONFIDENTIAL

Procedure:

1.

Download the FinCEN files in text format from the FinCEN website at http://www.fincen.gov.
The FinCEN files can be different for each organization. You may need to download a FinCEN People
file for individuals, a FinCEN Businesses file for businesses, or both. If you need to download both
files, then download a separate individual file and business file.

2.

In XG, create a custom screening list for each file if needed. Do not set an entity unique ID type.
You must create lists the first time that you set up your files for searching. For FinCEN file updates,
you only need to create a list if FinCEN now requires you to search both files.

3.

If you need to set up a business list, then use the following settings to import the file into the list:
File Format

FinCEN - Businesses

Reason Listed

FinCEN - Businesses

Chapter 7

M a na g em e nt Repor ts
Management reports can help you monitor your processing workflow and processing trends.
You can generate the following reports:
• The System History report shows the actions that were performed in a LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG
(XG) client instance.
• The Real-Time Searches Report shows the real-time searches that were performed.
• The Open Alert Age Report shows you how long open alerts have been in your review process.
• The Alert Status Report shows you the number alerts based on their current status.
• The Record Volume Report shows you summaries for the search service results that were generated.
• The Alert Viewed Not Worked Report shows you the alerts that were viewed but not processed.
• The Alerts Worked Report shows you the alerts that were processed.
• The Status Duration Report shows you how long alerts remained in each status of your workflow.
Statistics for alerts that were imported from another XG client instance or that were converted
from legacy products may not be included in the reports.

System History Report
The System History report provides a history of system activity that occurred in the XG application. The
report can be filtered by date, product area, and user.
The system history does not list actions taken through XG web services. In XG Enterprise, the system
history does not list actions taken though Enterprise Manager.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 209

CONFIDENTIAL

• The date range in which the action occurred.
• The product area where the action occurred.
• The user who took the action.

(Download).

Real-Time Searches Report
A Real-Time Searches Report provides a list of the real-time searches and the web service searches. The
report returns the search details, the alert ID if an alert was generated, and the number of screening list
matches.
This information can be used to monitor the real-time searches that each user performed and to provide
confirmation that a real-time search was performed and no matches were found.
Information from deleted alerts that were generated from real-time searches or web service searches
are still included in the Real-Time Searches report.

You can download the report as a PDF or as a CSV (comma-separated values) file.

exists.

Open Alert Age Report
Open Alert Age Reports show how long open alerts have been in your review process. The report can
help you monitor the age of open alerts for compliance purposes or to assess workloads on teams that
are processing the alerts. This information could be used to support process improvements or to justify
the need for additional training or resource allocation.
The alert totals for divisions and the overall alert total may be more than the actual number of
alerts due to possible overlap in the criteria that was used to return the alerts.

Generate an Open Alert Age Report
You can download the report as a PDF or as a CSV file.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Reports, and click Open Alert Age Report.

2.

Set the age ranges in days of the alerts.
The following tips may help you set the age ranges:
• To include today's alerts, enter 0. For example, 0 to 2 would find alerts that were created today,
yesterday, and the day before yesterday.
• You must enter the smaller of the two numbers in the left field and the larger of the two
numbers in the right field. For example, enter 0 to 30, not 30 to 0.
• Do not overlaps the ranges. For example, do not enter 0 to 7 and 7 to 14. Instead, enter 0 to
7 and 8 to 14.
• To view alerts that are older than a particular day, enter that number of days in the left field, and
leave the right field blank. For example, enter 30 in the left field to find all alerts that are older
than 30 days.

3.

Select the divisions of the users who can access the alerts.
Only divisions that you belong to are displayed. This option is not displayed if only one division
exists.

4.

Select how the alerts were distributed:
a. Select Roles, Users, Saved Query, or All.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 211

CONFIDENTIAL

b. If the field is available, then select the roles, the users, or the saved queries.
Only the users or the roles that contain users who belong to the selected divisions are displayed.
The report only lists the users, the roles, or the saved queries that were distributed alerts that meet
the selected criteria.

Select the file format for the report.

Click Download.

Status Duration Report
The Status Duration report helps you analyze the length of time that alerts spend at selected statuses.
The average time for the alerts spent at a status is calculated by adding the time the alerts were at the
status and dividing that number by the total number of status changes made to the alerts. You can use
this report to help analyze your processing workflow.
The report does not include the length of time alerts have spent in their current status.

Chapter 8

A dm i nis tr ation
You can control a variety of settings for system access and system setup.

Users
User accounts let you manage individual product access. You set the user to one role and at least one
division to control access within the product and for alert distribution.
Your organization can set password length and expiration requirements in the security policy.
®

®

When you initially set up LexisNexis Bridger Insight XG (XG), create divisions and roles before
you create user accounts. This setup order can help reduce the amount of navigation between
system access pages when you create user accounts.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 217

CONFIDENTIAL

For each user account, you can perform the following actions:
• Set the user account to only be used for web services.
• Allow XG to send email notifications to the user when open alerts are assigned to the user.
The email notification lets the user know that at least one alert was recently assigned to them or
their role. XG only sends one alert assignment notification within a one-hour time frame. After a user
receives a notification, XG does not send another alert assignment notification to the user until 60
minutes has lapsed no matter how many alerts are assigned to the user or their role in that time
period.
• Unlock user accounts that become locked after a set number of unsuccessful sign in attempts.
Locked user accounts display (Locked Account). Unlocked user accounts display (Unlocked
Account).
• Activate or suspend user accounts to control access to the product.
Users with suspended accounts cannot access the product, cannot receive open alert
assignments, and cannot receive email notifications. Suspending user accounts, instead of
deleting them, allows user accounts to remain in the system without being active in your
review process. For example, you can suspend an account for a user who is temporarily
assigned to other duties.
• Require password changes at the next sign in.
New users must change the password that was created by the product administrator the first time
that they sign in.
• View the sign-in history.
• Set the role to control access to the product functionality.
• Set the divisions to control access to accept lists, custom screening lists, results, alert decisions, and
predefined searches.
• Import user information to add multiple users to the system.
If you use Windows authentication to access XG Enterprise, then the following features are not
available:
• Accounts cannot be locked.
• Password changes cannot be required.
You can use the User Summary report to help you manage the user accounts.

Divisions on page 240
Roles on page 225
Security Policy on page 243

Add a User Account
You should create a user account for each user who accesses XG.
To view a training video about this task, see the training that is available on the LexisNexis® Risk
Solutions Customer Support at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Users.

2.

Click Add User.

3.

Enter a user name and a user ID.
If you use Windows authentication to access XG Enterprise, then enter the domain name.
User IDs need to meet the following requirements:
•
•
•
•
•
•

User IDs must be unique.
User IDs must contain at least eight characters.
User IDs must contain letters and numbers.
User IDs cannot contain any special characters other than hyphens (-) and underscores (_).
User IDs cannot contain the user's first name or last name.
User IDs can contain a number of repeating characters that is proportional to the ID length.
For example, an 8-character user ID can contain three repeating characters. Alternatively, a
15-character user ID can contain five repeating characters.

4.

If the client instance is an internal account, then enter the required employee ID.

5.

To create a user account that is only used for XG web services, select User for web services only.
This option is displayed only if web services are enabled for the client instance. The option is
activated only if IP settings are enabled in the client instance.
These credentials can only be used for XG web services. They cannot be used to access the
application. The password for the user account never expires. Be sure to keep this password
secure.

6.

Enter and confirm the user's email address.

7.

Enter and confirm a password.
A password is case sensitive and needs to meet the following requirements:
•
•
•
•
•

Your password must be 8–20 characters.
Your password must contain letters and numbers.
Your password must contain at least one special character (!, @, #, $, %, &, or *).
Your password cannot contain your user ID or the reverse of your user ID.
Your password cannot repeat any of the previous 12 passwords.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 219

CONFIDENTIAL

8.

To send the user email notifications when the user is assigned alerts, select Send the user an email
notification on alert assignment.
The email notification lets the user know that at least one alert was recently assigned to them or
their role. XG only sends one alert assignment notification within a one-hour time frame. After a
user receives a notification, XG does not send another alert assignment notification to the user until
60 minutes has lapsed no matter how many alerts are assigned to the user or their role in that time
period.

9.

Set the role.

10. Set the divisions.
The user must belong to at least one division.
11. Click Save.
After you complete this task:

Provide the credentials to the user.

Activate or Suspend a User Account
You activate or suspend a user account to help secure product access.
Before you begin this task:

Before you suspend a user account, reassign or process the user's assigned open alerts. If the user that
you want to suspend is selected as the responsible party or selected as the sole user to receive alerts in
any Automatic Batch configurations, then edit the configurations before you suspend the user.
Users with suspended accounts cannot access the system, cannot receive assigned open alerts, and
cannot receive email notifications.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Users.

2.

Select the user account that you want to activate or suspend.

3.

In the Account Status section, click Activate User or Suspend User.
To secure active accounts, you may want to reset the user's password and require the user to
change their password the next time that they sign in.

4.

Click Save.

(Suspended Account).

(Active Account).

Delete User Accounts

Before you delete a user account, you must reassign or process the user's assigned open alerts. If the

open alerts in any Automatic Batch configurations, then you must edit the configurations before you
