Roles
Roles help you ensure security and reduce training by limiting product access to the functionality that
users need to perform their required tasks.
You can use roles to help your business with the following tasks:
• Control access to product functionality.
• Limit access to saved queries, alert decisions, and predefined searches.
• Set up user groups for alert assignment workflow.
You can modify these roles or create new roles. For security purposes, create roles so that access is
limited to the functionality that users need to perform their required tasks. You can set only one role for
each user. Use careful consideration when creating roles and setting roles for users.
You can use the Role Summary report to help you manage the roles.
Related Information
Predefined Searches on page 251
Alert Processing on page 16

Privileges
Privileges control the role access to entire pages or to specific page options.
For example, you might give users in a product administrative role access to all functionality, but limit
users in a front-end role to only real-time searches.
You can select privileges to customize access for each role. Role privileges work in conjunction with the
access that is provided by a user's division.
Thoroughly test the role privileges to ensure that users who belong to the role have the access
that they need to perform their jobs.

S e a r c h M enu P rivil ege
The Search Menu privilege provides access to perform real-time searches.
When the privilege in this section is selected, the main menu displays the Search menu.
Real Time Search Forms
This privilege lets users perform real-time searches. The predefined searches that are listed on the
Search menu are based on the user's role access and division access.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 225

CONFIDENTIAL

Related Information
Real-Time Searches on page 36

Al e r t s M e nu P rivil eges
The Alerts Menu privileges provide access to alert queries and alert processing.
When privileges in this section are selected, the main menu displays the Alerts menu.
Alerts List
This privilege lets users view the saved queries that they have access to.
Edit Multiple Records
This privilege lets users edit multiple alerts at one time. When this privilege is selected, a check
box is displayed next to each alert, and alert decisions are displayed on the Alerts page.
Query
This privilege provides access to set up alert queries. You can configure the following options:
• The New Query option lets users create queries. When this option is selected, theAlerts
menu also displays the New Query button.
• The New Query, Save option lets users create and edit queries. When this option is selected,
the Alerts menu displays the Edit Queries button. The Refine Query button is displayed when
a saved query is selected.
Users in roles without the Share Query privilege can only edit their own personal
queries. They cannot edit shared queries.
Include Results Assigned To Others
This privilege lets users view the alerts that are assigned to other users or roles. When this
privilege is selected, the New Query page and the edit page display the option to view alerts
With any assignment in the Return alerts field.
Share Saved Queries
This privilege lets users share queries with other users and roles. When the privilege is
selected, the New Query page displays the Share Query option when a user edits a query.
The Alert Record privileges provide access to functionality for alert processing features.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 226

CONFIDENTIAL

Account Information
This privilege provides access to account information in the alerts. You can configure the following
options:
• The Read Only option lets you view the account information. When this option is selected, the
Record Details section is displayed on the Alert View page.
• The Edit option lets you edit the account information. When this option is selected, the Account
Information area displays the Save button.
Attachments
This privilege provides access to the file attachments in the alerts. You can configure the following
options:
• The Read Only option lets users view the file attachments. When this option is selected, the
Record Details section of the alert displays the files that are attached to the alert.
(Attach File)
• The Add option lets users add attachments. When this option is selected, the
icon displays on the Alert View page. In the classic alert view, the Record Details section of the
alert also displays the Attach File button.
• The Delete option lets users delete attachments. When this option is selected, the Records

Set Up a Role
You can create or edit a role. Each user account must belong to one role.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 238

CONFIDENTIAL

To view a training video about this task, see the training that is available on the Customer Support at
https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s.
Before you begin this task:

Identify the users who you want to belong to the role. After the role is created, you can only change the
users who belong to the role one at a time by editing each user account.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Roles.

2.

Click Add Role, or click the role that you want to edit.
Refer to the following image when you complete the next steps.

3.

Enter a unique name and a description.

4.

To send an email message to users when a single open alert is reassigned to their role, select Send
an email notification to users of this role on single alert reassignment.
The email notification lets the user know that at least one alert was recently assigned to them or
their role. XG only sends one alert assignment notification within a one-hour time frame. After a
user receives a notification, XG does not send another alert assignment notification to the user until
60 minutes has lapsed no matter how many alerts are assigned to the user or their role in that time
period.

5.

In the Privileges area, select the check boxes for the privileges that you want to grant to this role.

6.

Add users to the role.

7.

Click Save.

Related Information
Users on page 217
Privileges on page 225

Security Policy
To help secure XG access, you can configure the security policy that applies to user accounts.

Passwords
For passwords, you can set the following options:
• Minimum password length (8–20 characters)
• Password expiration frequency (1–90 days)
In addition to these settings, passwords must meet the requirements that are described in the XG
passwords section.

User Accounts
For user accounts, you can set the following options:
• The number of minutes that an account can be idle before the session times out (1–60 minutes)
• The number of days that an account can be inactive before the account is suspended and the
password must be reset (10–60 days)
• The number of sign-in attempts before the product locks the account (1–5 attempts)
If you use Windows authentication to access XG Enterprise, then you can configure only idle time outs.

Multi-Factor Authentication
For MFA (multi-factor authentication), you can set one of the following options to define how often users
must enter an email verification code (an OTP (one-time password)) at sign in:
• The first time that a user signs in from a new device
• Every time that a user signs in
You can also set the length of the email verification code.
MFA settings are available only if the feature is enabled for the XG client instance.
These settings do not affect web service access.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 243

CONFIDENTIAL

Single Sign On
If the client instance is configured to use SAML for SSO, then you can set XG to require that most users
sign into the product through SAML instead of through the standard sign-in page. Users who belong
to roles that let them edit the SAML IdP information and edit the security policy can still sign into the
product through the standard sign-in page.
This option does not affect web service access.
Related Information
Passwords on page 32

Change the Security Policy
You can change the options for the security policy.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Security Policy.

2.

Edit any options that you want to change.

3.

Click Save.

4.

Enter your password, and click OK.
XG lists the user who created the current security policy and the date and time that the user
created the policy.

After you complete this task:

You should notify users of any security policy changes that affect them.

SAML Identity Providers
XG offers SAML integration to let your organization's SSO ecosystem sign in users to XG and create user
accounts.
If you want to use a specific IdP for the client instance (not a multi-client IdP), then you set up
information for the IdP.
If a multi-client IdP is configured, this feature is not available in the application.
XG rejects SAML responses that contain expired certificates or certificates that do not match the
certificate that you add to your client instance. To help reduce the chance of service interruptions due to
expired security certificates that have not been replaced, XG lets you add up to two certificates.
XG can send email reminders when a certificate is about to expire. Reminders are sent 30 days, 7 days,
and 1 day before the certificate expires. XG sends the reminders to the email address that is associated
with the organization.
Before you can set up the information for the IdP, you need to configure your IdP to send SAML
responses to XG.
LexisNexis Risk Solutions does not assist you to set up an IdP.
For more information, see the SAML Integration for Single Sign-On in LexisNexis® Bridger Insight®
XG 5 technical reference guide at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/1662-SAML-forSingle-Sign-On-in-Bridger-Insight-XG-5.

Webhooks
Webhooks send real-time notifications from XG when specified events occur in the user interface, REST
API, or SOAP API.
Notifications can be sent for the following events:
• The alert state is closed for a single alert.
• An alert decision is applied to a single alert.
This event also includes a file being attached to or deleted from a single alert.
The notifications are sent as a JSON (JavaScript object notation) payload over HTTPS in a POST request to
the URL of your organization's receiving application. XG signs payloads with your provided HMAC (hashbased message authentication code) secret. This security feature allows you to verify the authenticity
and integrity of the payloads.
A payload is not sent when alerts are closed or alert decisions are applied through a multiple entity
process or through batch processing.
Your personnel needs the skills to set up the receiving application and manage the JSON payloads.
LexisNexis Risk Solutions does not assist with the support of the receiving application.
Webhooks functionality is only available if configured for your client instance. XG Service clients should
contact Customer Support.
For more information about webhooks, see the Webhooks for LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG 5
implementation guide at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/3289.

Add a Webhook
You need the payload URL and the secret from the receiving application to add a webhook.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Webhooks.

2.

Click Add Webhook.

3.

Enter a unique name.

4.

Select the webhook event.

5.

Enter the payload URL.

6.

Enter the secret from the receiving application.

7.

To activate the webhook, select Active.

8.

Click Save Webhook.

Predefined Searches
Predefined searches provide a specific set of settings that XG uses to perform searches. Automating the
selection of these search settings helps you establish more efficient and consistent searching.
You can create multiple predefined searches to meet your processing needs. For example, you can set
up several predefined searches to search against different combinations of search categories, such as
Sanctions, PEP (politically exposed person), or Adverse Media. Alternatively, you could set up predefined
searches that are only available to users in particular divisions or in particular roles.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 251

CONFIDENTIAL

You can configure the following settings for predefined searches:
•
•
•
•

Set the predefined search access.
Configure the input fields for real-time searches.
Configure alert distribution for real-time searches.
Configure the LexisNexis Risk Solutions list screening service to search LexisNexis Risk Solutions lists
and LexisNexis® WorldCompliance™ lists.
• Configure the additional LexisNexis Risk Solutions search services.
Predefined searches affect the alerts that the product generates. To help reduce internal risk,
carefully assess which users have access to set up and use predefined searches.

Predefined searches are available for a search only when they meet the following criteria:
• The entity type of the input data is supported by the selected search services.
For example, input records with an unknown entity type cannot be searched by certain search
services.
• The input data meets the requirements of the selected search services.
For example, input records with only a full name cannot be searched by certain search services.
• The user has access to the predefined search based on division access and role access.

Predefined Search Settings for List Screening
Predefined searches include settings that you can configure for the list screening service.
The list screening service lets you search your input entities against the screening lists that are provided
by LexisNexis Risk Solutions and the WorldCompliance lists that your organization purchased access to.
You can configure the following settings for the list screening service:
• List options that affect the search that is performed on a particular list
• Search options that affect each search that is performed
Many of these options affect how XG identifies possible matches.
These settings can affect search performance and results. Test different settings to determine the
settings that best suit your company's processing needs and risk tolerance.

L i s t O p t i on s
To perform a search in the list screening service, you must select the screening lists, custom screening
lists, and accept lists that you want to search. Depending on the lists that you select, you can configure
a number of settings that control the search that is performed on those lists and the matches that are
reported.
Minimum Scores
For each screening list and each custom screening list that is added to a predefined search, you can
set the minimum value for the match confidence score that is required for XG to report the matches in
alerts.
XG provides a match confidence score between 70–100 for each match.The score indicates how closely
the input entity matched the screening list entity. The score is not a percentage. A score of 90 indicates a
closer match than a score of 80.
Certain XG client instances may still be configured to provide a match confidence score between
50–100. However, LexisNexis Risk Solutions recommends that you use at least a minimum score of
70 for optimal results.
You can also set a default minimum score that automatically sets the minimum score for each list that
you add to a predefined search. You can apply the default minimum score to all lists that you previously
added to a predefined search. You can also change the minimum score for each screening list.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 257

CONFIDENTIAL

Lower minimum score thresholds may increase the matches that are reported. Test different
settings to determine the scores that best suit your organization's risk tolerance.
Related Information
Weak AKA Names on page 258
Search Criteria on page 258
Configure the Search Settings for List Screening on page 270
Weak AKA Names
Some source agencies identify low-quality AKA names that are relatively broad and generic as a weak
AKA in their list records. An example of a weak AKA name is “Hassan the Old” because the name and the
descriptor are both common terms.
For certain screening lists, you can set XG to ignore weak AKA names in list records. This option lets you
focus the search on higher-quality entity information. This option may also help reduce the number of
false positive matches that XG reports. This functionality is available for the following lists:
•
•
•
•

OFAC SDN (specially designated nationals) list
OFAC Non-SDN Entities list
Ukraine Financial Monitoring list
Some WorldCompliance lists

Related Information
Minimum Scores on page 257
Search Criteria on page 258
Configure the Search Settings for List Screening on page 270
Search Criteria
The search criteria functionality offers granular filtering possibilities that can help you process
information more effectively and efficiently by searching only the list records that are most likely to
contain information that is relevant to your business needs.
You can select various search criteria to focus on the relevant records. For the WorldCompliance lists,
you select search criteria that is organized by groups. For the legacy LexisNexis® WorldCompliance™ Data
list, you determine the AND/OR logic that is used for the search criteria. For the UN Consolidated List,
you select the relevant search criteria. For example, you only want to search Iran and Iraq records in the
UN Consolidated List. You select the Iran and Iraq search criteria. XG does not search the list records
from unselected values.
The use of search criteria may reduce the number of reported matches. Thoroughly test the use of
search criteria based on your organization's risk tolerance before you implement this functionality
into your alert processes.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 258

CONFIDENTIAL

For more information about the ways you can use search criteria, see the following documentation that
is available on the LexisNexis® Risk Solutions Customer Support Hub:
• Search Criteria for the Legacy LexisNexis® WorldCompliance™ Lists in LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG
technical reference guide at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2045
• Search Criteria for the LexisNexis® WorldCompliance™ Data Plus List in LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG
5 technical white paper at https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2493

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 259

CONFIDENTIAL

General Options
General options can affect how XG generates an alert, how the match confidence score is determined,
and what comparisons are made during the search.
The following general options are available for list screening searches:
Scan name fields for country names
This option sets XG to search name fields for certain data in country lists. This data includes country
names, country AKA names, country terms (for example, Iranian), cities, and ports.
For example, you perform a search that contains Bank of Iran as the input name. XG would report
a potential match against a country list that contains Iran.
Set alert state to open for records with errors
This option sets XG to generate an open alert when an error occurs during the search.
Ignore matches against vessels
This option sets XG to not report name matches for list entities with a vessel entity type. If you do
not conduct business with entities that are associated with vessels, then you might choose to select
this option to help reduce the false positives that are reported.
Scan run-together words for country names
This option sets XG to search input run-together words for country names that are included in
country lists.
Scan address fields for country names
This option sets XG to search the Address Line 1 input field and the Address Line 2 input field for
certain data in country lists, but only if data is not provided in the City input field, the State input
field, or the Country input field. This data includes country names, country AKA names, country
terms (for example, Iranian), cities, and ports.
This option is designed to find country data in unparsed addresses when the country name is
provided in an input address field other than the Country field. For example, you select this option
and enter 1 Cuba Street, Anytown, AA 00012 in the Address Line 1 field. You search against a
country list that contains Cuba. XG would report a potential match.
If data is provided in any other address fields, then XG searches the data as a parsed address,
which may return different results.
Increase the score when the first name or the middle name is an initial
This option sets XG to increase the score when the first name or the middle name is an initial.
For example, you search your input entity Imaginerry T Person against a custom list that contains
Imaginary Test Person. XG returns a score of 88 if this option is not selected. XG returns a score of
92 if this option is selected.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 260

CONFIDENTIAL

This option may also increase the score if an alternative name for the input name matches a
first-name initial or a middle-name initial in the entity name on the list. For example, you search your
input entity Patricia Test Person against a custom list that contains T Test Person. XG returns a
higher score if this option is selected because the alternative names for Patricia (Trisha or Trish)
matched T in the entity name on the custom list.
Increase scores for single-word organization names
This option sets XG to increase the score for matches on single-word organization names. For
example, this option may increase scores for matches on acronyms.
Related Information
Configure the Search Settings for List Screening on page 270
Match Options on page 261
Payment Screening Options on page 262
Rules for Automatic False Positives on page 263
Match Decisions and Match Updates on page 268
Match Options
The match options set XG to use addresses, IDs, and phone numbers in addition to name to find
candidate records in parsed data. Match options are not applied to searches that are processed using the
XG - Unstructured format.
These options increase the scope of your search and can decrease the speed of the search.
For consistent results, you should consider the following for your searches:
• In real-time searches, set the fields that are affected by your selected match options as required
fields.
• In batch searches, include the fields that are affected by your selected match options in your files.
• In web services, include the properties that are affected by your selected match options in your
requests.
Related Information
Configure the Search Settings for List Screening on page 270
General Options on page 260

Match Decisions and Match Updates on page 268

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 261

CONFIDENTIAL

Payment Screening Options
Payment screening options let you configure XG to search each field independently in payment data
records for certain data element matches.
The following payment screening options are available:
Scan all fields for names
This option sets the LexisNexis® Search Core to search input fields for entity names.
Scan all fields for country names
This option sets the LexisNexis Search Core to search input fields for country names.
Scan all fields for country codes
This option sets the LexisNexis Search Core to search input fields for country codes. Two-character
and three-character country codes from ISO (International Organization for Standardization) are
supported. You can scan for country codes only if you scan for country names.
Scan all fields for SWIFT BICs
This option sets the LexisNexis Search Core to search input fields for a SWIFT (Society for Worldwide
Interbank Financial Telecommunication) BIC (Business Identifier Code).

ACH Options
You can set how XG handles IAT (International Automated Clearing House Transaction) records.
The IAT structure includes two U.S. OFAC indicators. These indicators are used to communicate that
an OFAC match was found for one of the entities that is associated with the transaction by screeners
that are external to XG. Typically, XG reports a match if the input IAT record contains either of these
indicators. For records that contain both indicators, XG creates only one alert. XG reports the match
against the originating entity. If the originating entity is not included in the record, then XG reports the
match against the first parsed entity. Along with the match that is reported because of the indicators, XG
also reports any additional matches for entities that are associated with the record.
You can set XG to not report matches when these indicators are present. The following ACH (Automated
Clearing House) options are available:
Ignore Gateway Operator OFAC Screening Indicator
This option sets XG to not generate an alert when an input ACH record contains a gateway operator
OFAC screening indicator.
Ignore Secondary OFAC Screening Indicator
This option sets XG to not generate an alert when an input ACH record contains a secondary OFAC
screening indicator.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 262

CONFIDENTIAL

Rules for Automatic False Positives
Rules for automatic false positives can help you automate review decisions that are obvious or clerical.
XG offers standard rules and LexisNexis® Intelligent Match Decision Solution (IMDS) to help you
automate some aspects of false positive processing. You use these rules to identify false positives
without manually reviewing the match based on clear differences between the input entity and the
match entity (for example, different genders).
You should not use the standard rules for automatic false positives in combination with rules for
IMDS.

Standard Rules
You can set the standard rules to determine that a list match in an alert is an automatic false positive
when only the input entity name matches a list entity name and the specified data element does not
match. You can also set XG to consider a list match in an alert to be an automatic false positive when the
input name matches a list entity name and the list match meets the White List criteria.
These rules are not applied to searches that are processed with the XG - Unstructured format.
You use the XG - Unstructured format to process files with unparsed data that is not provided in
defined fields. Because XG cannot distinguish between addresses, IDs, or other data elements in
unparsed data, XG searches for only names in these files.
The following standard rules are available:
Date of Birth
This option sets XG to consider a list match in an alert to be an automatic false positive when the
following criteria is met:
• The input name matches a list entity name.
• The following data elements do not match in the list match: address, DOB, ID number, or phone
number.
• The input DOB does not match the DOB of the list entity.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 263

CONFIDENTIAL

Tolerance
This option works with the Date of Birth rule. The option specifies how many months an input
DOB can vary from the DOB of a list entity before XG applies the rules for an automatic false
positive.
For example, the DOB of a list entity is 4/15/1950. If you enter 2 in the Tolerance field, then
an input DOB between 2/15/1950 and 6/15/1950 does not activate the Automatic False Positive
rules because the DOB is too varied.
IDs
This option sets XG to consider a list match in an alert to be an automatic false positive when the
following criteria is met:
• The input name matches a list entity name.
• The following data elements do not match in the list match: address, DOB, ID number, or phone
number.
• The input ID does not match the ID of the list entity.
Gender
This option sets XG to consider a list match in an alert to be an automatic false positive when the
following criteria is met:
• The input name matches a list entity name.
• The following data elements do not match in the list match: address, DOB, ID number, or phone
number.
• The input gender does not match the gender of the list entity.
Addresses
This option sets XG to consider a list match in an alert to be an automatic false positive when the
following criteria is met:
• The input name matches a list entity name.
• The following data elements do not match in the list match: address, DOB, ID number, or phone
number.
• The input address does not match the address of the list entity.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 264

CONFIDENTIAL

Countries
This option sets XG to consider a list match in an alert to be an automatic false positive when the
following criteria is met:
• The input name matches a list entity name.
• The following data elements do not match in the list match: address, DOB, ID number, or phone
number.
• The input country does not match the country of the list entity.
Only country names in English, for both the input country and list entity country, are currently
supported for this rule to work properly and avoid alerts from being incorrectly suppressed.
When the list record contains multiple countries and a partial address with no country,
country matches are not identified as automatic false positives. For example, an input
record contains United States as a country. The list record contains United States as
a country and a partial address of 100 Main St, Dallas, Texas. The country would
not be identified as an automatic false positive, because the partial address is missing a
country to match against.
Phone Numbers
This option sets XG to consider a list match in an alert to be an automatic false positive when the
following criteria is met:
• The input name matches a list entity name.
• The following data elements do not match in the list match: address, DOB, ID number, or phone
number.
• The input phone number does not match the phone number of the list entity.
Entity Type
This option sets XG to consider a list match in an alert to be an automatic false positive when the
following criteria is met:
• The input name matches a list entity name.
• The following data elements do not match in the list match: address, DOB, ID number, or phone
number.
• The input entity type does not match the entity type of the list entity.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 265

CONFIDENTIAL

Citizenship
This option sets XG to consider a list match in an alert to be an automatic false positive when the
following criteria is met:
• The input name matches a list entity name.
• The following data elements do not match in the list match: address, DOB, ID number, or phone
number.
• The input citizenship does not match the citizenship of the list entity.

Intelligent Match Decision Solution
IMDS lets your organization develop rules to automatically process list matches in a way that aligns with
your organization's list screening program and risk profile. The rules directly utilize input, list, and match
attributes from XG searches to test for evidence of a false positive. IMDS uses specified rules and a
confidence threshold to determine whether a match is an automatic false positive. Successful outcomes
in a well-planned, tuned, and validated implementation of IMDS can result in increased productivity and
reduced operational costs.
IMDS is available based on your product subscription. Before you can configure IMDS in a
predefined search, the rules must be set up in the system for your XG client instance. For XG
®
®
Enterprise, see LexisNexis Bridger Insight XG Enterprise Manager Help.
If IMDS is configured for your client instance, then you can set the rules and the confidence threshold
that a match must meet to be considered an automatic false positive. The false positive confidence score
indicates how confident the rules are that the match is a false positive. The false positive confidence
score can range from 0.0000 (no confidence that the match is a false positive) to 10.0000 (full confidence
that the match is a false positive).
The false positive confidence score is not the same as the match confidence score (70-100) that XG
provides for each match to indicate how closely the list entity matches the input entity.
For more information about rules for IMDS, see the Rules for LexisNexis® Intelligent Match Decision
Solution technical reference guide.

Application of the Rules
You can set multiple rules for automatic false positives. A list match needs to meet only one of the
specified rules for XG to determine that the match is an automatic false positive. However, if any of the
following data elements also matches in the same list match, then the product does not set the match as
an automatic false positive: address, DOB, ID number, or phone number.
An alert can contain multiple list matches. When only some list matches in the alert meet one of the
specified rules, XG generates an alert with an open alert state. By default, this alert contains only the
list matches that do not meet a rule. You can configure the product to also include the list matches that
meet a rule in the alert.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 266

CONFIDENTIAL

When all list matches in the alert meet one of the selected rules, XG generates an alert with an open
alert state by default. You can configure the product to not generate an alert or to generate an alert with
an Unassigned alert state.
Before alerts with an Unassigned alert state can be set to Closed, the alert state must first be
changed to Open.
Automatic False Positive Example

Your organization decides that matches are false positives when the input entity’s gender and the list
entity’s gender are not the same. You specify the standard rule for gender in the settings that you use to
search your input entity.
You search the following input entity:
Name: Zach Thul
Gender: Female
Address: 503 Waybreeze Blvd

XG finds this list entity match:
Name: Zach Thul
Gender: Male
Address: 111 Waybreeze Blvd

The gender does not match so XG considers the match to be an automatic false positive. However, if the
address had matched, then XG would not consider the match to be an automatic false positive.
If the alert contains only list matches that meet the Automatic False Positive rule for gender, then the
predefined search sets XG to complete one of the following actions:
• The product generates an alert with an open alert state.
• The product generates an alert with an unassigned alert state.
• The product does not generate an alert.
If the alert contains list matches that do not meet the rule, then XG generates an alert with an open alert
state by default. The alert contains the list matches that do not meet the rule. The predefined search
tells the product whether the alert can also contain the list matches that do meet the rule.

Automatic False Positive De-duplication
XG applies automatic false positive de-duplication to qualified alerts. This feature is designed to help
reduce alert volumes and conserve database space.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 267

CONFIDENTIAL

The automatic false positive is not reported when the input entity information, list matches, and
divisions for the alert match an automatic false positive in an existing alert. In addition, the same
automatic false positive rules must be true for the existing alert and the duplicate alert. Qualified alerts
must meet the following criteria:
• The input entity information is standard, parsed data (not payment transaction data or unstructured
data).
• The alert status is set to Automatic False Positive.
• The alert assignment is set to Unassigned.
• The alert state is set to Unassigned.
This feature is enabled by default for clients who were new subscribers after March 2022. Legacy
clients can request that the feature be enabled.
In the alert in the new alert view, the duplicate automatic false positive history contains the previous 25
duplicate instances.

Match Decisions and Match Updates
Match decisions are used to separately resolve each match in an alert. Match updates notify you of
changes to previously reviewed matches that were added to an accept list.

Match Decisions
When match decisions are configured, you can set each list match in an alert as a true match or as a
false positive. Your process settings may require that all the matches in an alert be set to false positive
before a user can set a specific alert status in an alert decision. For example, you may let users set a
Transaction Approved alert status only after they have determined that all matches in the alert are
false positive.
In the new alert view, this option sets XG to display the
icon, and the

(False Positive) icon, the

(True Match)

(Unknown) icon for each match in an alert.

In the classic alert view, this option sets XG to display the (False Positive) icon and the
(True Match)
icon for each match in an alert. Users must set a match decision for each match before they can close
the alert or add the alert to an accept list.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 268

CONFIDENTIAL

You may want to conduct business with entities that are processed using match decisions. You should
consider using a predefined search and an accept list for profile processing that is separate from the
predefined searches and the accept lists that you use for sanctions processing.

Match Updates
Match updates notify you when changes occur to a match in an accept list record. For XG to generate
match updates, the predefined search must be configured to generate match updates and include the
accept list that contains the record.
XG can be set to generate an alert that contains a true match update when list entity information
changes for a true match in an accept list record.
True match updates are designed for profile monitoring and alert you to changes in the profiles of
true matches that may lead you to reassess your previous risk level designation. This functionality
is not designed for processing sanctions list matches. Due to regulations or high risk, you most likely do
not want to conduct business with the entities that are on a sanctions list.
XG does not generate a true match update when changes occur only to the following profile
information: the entity unique ID, the reference ID, the date that the profile was listed, or the date
that the profile was modified.
XG can be set to generate an alert that contains a false match update when new match information is
found for certain data elements that are in an accept list record. You can also set the default settings that
are used for all predefined searches.
You can select the following data elements to generate a false match update:
•
•
•
•

Address
AKA
DOB
Citizenship

•
•
•
•

Gender
ID Numbers
Name
Phone

For a match that was found on a custom screening list, XG can only generate a false match update
if the list is required to contain a unique ID for each record.
False match updates are designed to alert you to new match information that may need further
investigation to determine whether the record should remain on the accept list as a false positive. For
example, if you previously added a match to an accept list that did not contain a matching DOB, and then
XG found a matching DOB in a later search, XG would generate a false match update.

Predefined Search Settings for FraudPoint Score
To search the FraudPoint Score service, you add the service to predefined searches and configure the
search settings. XG performs the search simultaneously with the other services that are included in the
predefined search.
You can also use the predefined search to configure the settings for service searches that a user may
perform after the alert is generated. You configure the search settings, but you do not add the service
to the predefined search. If you do not configure the service settings in the predefined search, then the
service uses its default settings to perform the search.
You can include the LexisNexis® Red Flags Rule Report in your FraudPoint Score searches at an additional
cost. This report can help comply with the Fair and Accurate Credit Transactions (FACT) Act Identity Theft
Red Flags Rule by revealing patterns, practices, and suspicious activities that may indicate the possibility
of identity theft.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 274

CONFIDENTIAL

S e a r c h S et tin g s f or FraudPoi nt Sc ore
The settings for individual entities are configured in a predefined search. Searches that meet multiple
alert thresholds generate only one alert.
General - Alert Thresholds
• LexisNexis® FraudPoint® Model: 2.0 or 1.0
• If 2.0 is selected as the FraudPoint Model, then you can configure the following options:
• Generate an open alert if FraudPoint Score is less than or equal to the selected value (300–
999).
• Generate an open alert if the Synthetic Identity index is greater than or equal to the selected
value (1–9).
• Generate an open alert if the Stolen Identity index is greater than or equal to the selected
value (1–9).
• Generate an open alert if the Manipulated Identity index is greater than or equal to the
selected value (1–9).
• Generate an open alert if the Vulnerable Victim index is greater than or equal to the selected
value (1–9).
• Generate an open alert if the Friendly Fraud index is greater than or equal to the selected
value (1–9).
• Generate an open alert if the Suspicious Activity index is greater than or equal to the selected
value (1–9).
• Generate an alert when a search error is returned.
• Generate an alert if any of the selected warning codes is returned.
Red Flags
• Include the Red Flags Rule Report (additional charges may apply).
• Generate an alert if any of the selected red flags is returned.
Search Options
Only perform the search if an IP address is present or if a current address and a mailing address are
both present.
The mailing address is used in the search instead of the current address. Most users do not
use this option.

Red Flags Rule Report
The FACTA (Fair and Accurate Credit Transactions Act) Identity Theft Red Flags Rule may require you to
evaluate the effectiveness of your existing prevention, detection, and response capabilities to respond to
fraud and create or update policies and procedures to improve your processes.
The Red Flags Rule Report can help you comply with the FACT Act Identity Theft Red Flags Rule by
revealing patterns, practices, and suspicious activities that may indicate the possibility of identity theft.
You can configure the search to return a Red Flags Rule Report.
Red Flags
XG can be configured to generate an open alert when FraudPoint Score returns at least one red flag.
The service can return the following red flags:

Predefined Search Settings for InstantID
To search the InstantID service, you add the service to predefined searches and configure the search
settings. XG performs the search simultaneously with the other services that are included in the
predefined search.
You can also use the predefined search to configure the settings for service searches that a user may
perform after the alert is generated. You configure the search settings, but you do not add the service
to the predefined search. If you do not configure the service settings in the predefined search, then the
service uses its default settings to perform the search.
You can configure settings for individual searches and business searches.

I n di v i d u al Search Settings for Ins tant ID
The settings for individual entities are configured in a predefined search. Searches that meet multiple
alert thresholds generate only one alert.
General - Alert Thresholds
• Generate an open alert when the InstantID index is less than or equal to a specified value.
• Generate an open alert when InstantID returns a search error.
Risk Indicators
Generate an open alert when InstantID returns a selected risk indicator.
Red Flags
• Include a Red Flags Rule Report.
• Generate an open alert when InstantID returns a selected Red Flag condition.
NAS (name, address, and SSN) and NAP (name, address, and phone number) Criteria
Generate an open alert when search results are less than or equal to the InstantID index that is
selected to generate an alert, and equal to the selected NAS value or the selected NAP value.

Search Options
•
•
•
•
•

Set the index to 10 when the address contains a post office box number.
Set the index to 10 when more than one SSN is associated with the input entity.
Set the index to 10 when multiple identities are associated with the input SSN.
Include the DOB verification in the index calculation.
Include the driver license verification in the index calculation.
If the DOB or the driver license is included in the search and one or both are verified, then
the index can increase by 10. However, the verification of one or both of these elements
cannot increase the index from a 40 to a 50, or the verification cannot increase the index
if an index override option is selected. The index is not lowered if the DOB or the driver
license cannot be verified.

• Set the index to 10 when the input SSN is not the primary SSN for the input entity.
• Return all risk indicators that are found in the search instead of only the top six risk indicators.
• Set the number of months since the input identity was last seen at the input address to consider
the address as verified.
• Set the InstantID version that you want to use in the search.
Version 0 is retired. If this option is selected, then Version 1 is used.
Set the InstantID service to require exact matches on the following input information:
• Last Name
• First Name
• First Name Allow Nickname
For example, Mike may be considered a
match for Michael.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

• Home Phone
• SSN

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 283

CONFIDENTIAL

Set one of the following options for the logic that is used to determine DOB matches:
• Fuzzy Match CCYYMMDD searches for close matches to the year, month, and day of birth of the
input DOB.
For example, a search on an input DOB of 12/15/1955 may return results with a DOB of
12/15/1954, 11/ 15/1955, or 12/14/1955.
• Fuzzy Match CCYYMM searches for close matches to the year and month of birth of the input
DOB.
For example, a search on an input DOB of 12/15/1955 may return results with a DOB of 12/DD/
1954 or 11/DD/1955. The day of birth does not affect results.
• Exact CCYYMMDD searches for exact matches to the year, month, and day of birth of the input
DOB.
For example, a search on an input DOB of 12/15/1955 DOB returns only results with a DOB of
12/15/1955.
• Exact CCYYMM searches for exact matches to the year and month of birth of the input DOB.
For example, a search on an input DOB of 12/15/1955 returns only results with a DOB of 12/DD/
1955.
• Radius Match CCYY searches for any DOB within a specified range of years of the input DOB. You
can set the range between 0–3 years.
For example, you set the radius to 2 years. A search on an input DOB of 12/15/1955 may return
results with a DOB between MM/DD/1953 and MM/DD/1957.
Related Information
Configure the Search Settings for InstantID on page 292
Comprehensive Verification Index
InstantID returns a CVI (comprehensive verification index) for each search.
You can set XG to generate an open alert when InstantID returns the selected index value.
Index Values
Value

Description

0

Nothing verified

10

Critical ID elements not verified, associated with different people, or
indicate potential risk such as deceased/invalid SSN, SSN issued prior to
input DOB, etc.

20

Minimal verification, critical ID elements not verified or associated with
different person(s)

30

Several ID elements verified

40

Last name, address and SSN or phone verified; first name, phone or SSN
verification failures

50

Full name, address, phone, SSN verified

Red Flags Rule Report
The FACTA Identity Theft Red Flags Rule may require you to evaluate the effectiveness of your existing
prevention, detection, and response capabilities to respond to fraud and create or update policies and
procedures to improve your processes.
The Red Flags Rule Report can help you comply with the FACT Act Identity Theft Red Flags Rule by
revealing patterns, practices, and suspicious activities that may indicate the possibility of identity theft.
You can configure the search to return a Red Flags Rule Report.

Alert Decision Setup
Alert decisions let you provide a specific set of actions that users can take on alerts.
Users can apply an alert decision that they can access to a single alert or to selected alerts in an alert
list. By automating some case management actions, you can help prevent decision-making errors and
establish more efficient and consistent review processes.
Alert decisions work in conjunction with process settings to help you establish consistently-applied
review processes. Process settings can override settings that are configured in an alert decision. For
example, an alert decision is configured initially to require that the user set a status, but not add a note.
However, the process settings require that the user add a note when they set a status. In this case, the
alert decision requires that the user add a note.
Related Information
Set Up an Alert Decision on page 296
Alert Statuses on page 302
Decision Tags on page 303

Alert Decision Options
You can set a variety of alert decision options for alert management.
Assignment Options
You can set the following actions for the alert assignment:
•
•
•
•
•
•
•

Do not let the user change the alert assignment.
Let the user assign the alert.
Require the user to assign the alert.
Clear the assignment.
Assign the alert to a specific role.
Assign the alert to a specific user.
Assign the alert to the current user.

If the user is prompted or required to assign the alert, then the alert decision displays only the users
who belong to the division that can access the alert. Alternatively, the alert decision displays only the
roles that have users who belong to the division that can access the alert.
If you set the alert assignment as part of the alert decision, then only the users who belong to the
divisions that you belong to are displayed. Alternatively, only the roles that have users who belong to
the divisions that you belong to are displayed.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 293

CONFIDENTIAL

Status Options
You can set the following actions for the alert status:
•
•
•
•
•

Do not let the user change the status.
Let the user set the status.
Require the user to set the status.
Clear the status.
Set the alert to a specific status.

State Options
You can set the following actions for the alert state:
• Do not let the user change the state.
• Require the user to set the state.
• Set the alert to a specific state.
Accept List Options
You can set the following actions for an accept list:
•
•
•
•

Do not let the user add the alert to a list.
Let the user add the alert to a list.
Require the user to add the alert to a list.
Add the alert to a specific list.

If the user is prompted or required to select a list, then the alert decision displays only the lists that
the user can access based on the user's divisions.
If you set the list as part of the alert decision, then only the lists that you can access based on your
divisions are displayed.
Custom Screening List Options
You can set the following actions for a custom screening list:
•
•
•
•

Do not let the user add the alert to a list.
Let the user add the alert to a list.
Require the user to add the alert to a list.
Add the alert to a specific list.

If the user is prompted or required to select a list, then the alert decision displays only the lists that
the user can access based on the user's divisions.
If you set the list as part of the alert decision, then only the lists that you can access based on your
divisions are displayed.

•
•
•
•

•
•
•
•

Allow the user to enter a note.
Require the user to enter a note.
Add a specific note.

Navigation Options
You can set the following actions for the alert navigation:
• Let the user decide the navigation.
• Set the product to move to the next available alert after the user applies the alert decision.
• Set the product to remain on the alert that the user applies the alert decision to.
You can choose to let the user apply the alert decision to a single alert in one click when no
additional user input is necessary. For example, this option may be helpful when the sole purpose of
the alert decision is to assign the alert to the current user. When this option is selected, XG applies
the alert decision without displaying its options and either remains on the alert or moves to the next
alert.
Division Access Options
This option sets access to the alert decision based on the divisions that the user belongs to.
Only the divisions that you belong to are displayed. This option is not available if you only belong to
one division.
Role Access Options
This option sets access to the alert decision based on the role of the user.
Only the roles that contain users who belong to the selected divisions are displayed.
Predefined Search Access Options
This option sets access to the alert decision based on the predefined search that generated the alert.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 295

CONFIDENTIAL

Only the predefined searches that you can access based on your divisions and based on your role are
displayed. Also, only the predefined searches that can be accessed by the selected divisions and the
selected roles are displayed.
Related Information
Set Up an Alert Decision on page 296

Set Up an Alert Decision
You can create or edit alert decisions to manage your alert processing.
To view a training video about this task, see the training that is available on the Customer Support at
https://lnrs.force.com/CustomerSupportHub/s.
Your process settings or list settings may affect the options that the users can apply in alert decisions.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Alert Decisions.

2.

Click Add Decision, or click an existing alert decision to edit.

3.

Enter a unique name and a description.

4.

If the option is available, then set the action for the following items:
• Alert assignment
• Alert status
• Alert state
• Accept list
• Custom screening list
• Decision tags
• Note
• Alert navigation

5.

Set the access to the alert decision based on the divisions, roles, and predefined searches.

6.

Click Save.

Result:

If the user has access to the alert decision, then XG displays the alert decision for an alert list when the
user selects alerts.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 296

CONFIDENTIAL

Delete Alert Decisions
You can delete alert decisions that are no longer applicable to your review processes.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Alert Decisions.

2.

Select the alert decision that you want to delete by using one of the following methods:
• Select the check box next to the alert decision that you want to delete, and click (Delete).
This method lets you delete multiple alert decisions at one time.
• Click the alert decision to open the edit page, and click (Delete).

3.

Click Yes.

Result:

XG no longer displays the alert decision for an alert list when you select alerts or when you view a single
alert.
Related Information
Alert Decision Setup on page 293

Alert View Field Sets
Alert view field sets let you control the columns for list screening results that are displayed in an alert.
Field sets provide a streamlined summary of all the matches that were reported in the alert. This feature
is not available in the classic alert view.
You create the field sets as part of your administrative tasks. XG displays the field set when the user
views a single alert or generates an alert report. You can control whether users can access the field set
based on the roles that are assigned to the alerts, the predefined searches that generated the alerts, and
the results that the alerts contain.
Alerts can contain true match updates. The True Match Update Updates option sets XG to display the
field set when the viewed alerts contain true match updates.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 297

CONFIDENTIAL

Alerts can also contain list screening matches. The following options for list screening matches are
available:
• The List Screening Matches option sets XG to display the field set when the viewed alerts contain any
of the following types of data: parsed, unparsed, or payment transaction.
• The Payment Matches option sets XG to display the field set when unparsed data or any of the
following types of payment transaction data: ACH data, Fedwire data, ISO 20022, and SWIFT.
• The FEDWIRE Matches option sets XG to display the field set when the viewed alerts contain Fedwire
data.
• The ISO 20022 Matches option sets XG to display the field set when the viewed alerts contain ISO
20022 data.
• The SWIFT Matches option sets the field sets XG to display the field set when the viewed alerts
contain SWIFT data.
• The Unstructured Matches option sets XG to display the field set when the viewed alerts contain
unparsed data.
Alerts can also contain user-provided notes in the details of each match when the information is
specifically relevant to the match instead of the alert in general. To help ensure users are aware of
the notes, you can add the field to an alert view field set.

Set Up an Alert View Field Set
You can create and edit alert view field sets to meet your processing needs.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Alert View Field Sets.

2.

Click Add Field Set, or click a field set to edit.

3.

Enter a unique name.

4.

Set the fields:
• To add a field, click Add Field, and select the field.
• To remove a field, click the X that corresponds to the field.
• To change the field order, drag and drop the field into the desired position.

5.

Set the access to the field set based on the roles that are assigned to the alerts.

6.

Set the access to the field set based on the predefined searches that generate the alerts.

7.

Set the access to the field set based on the results that the alerts contain.

8.

Click Save.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 298

CONFIDENTIAL

Delete Alert View Field Sets
You can delete alert view field sets that are no longer applicable to your review processes.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Alert View Field Sets.

2.

Select the field set that you want to delete by using one of the following methods:
• Select the check box next to the field set that you want to delete, and click (Delete).
This method lets you delete multiple field sets at one time.
• Click the field set to open the edit page, and click (Delete).

3.

Click Yes.

Result:

XG no longer displays the deleted field set when you view a single alert or when you generate alert
reports.

Match Indicator Ranges
Match indicator ranges let you determine which match indicator is displayed based on the score that was
calculated for each data element match. This feature is not available in the classic alert view.
Match indicators are quick visual cues about the likelihood of the data element match based on the
analysis conducted by the LexisNexis Search Core. The ranges let you control the significance of a data
element match based on your review processes.

Set Up Match Indicator Ranges
You can set up the score ranges for each data element to return a specific type of match indicator.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Match Indicator Ranges.

2.

For each available data element, enter a value (1–100) for the no match indicator and the match
indicator.

3.

For the DOB element, enter the number of months (1–100) that the DOB in the list record can vary
from the input DOB.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 299

CONFIDENTIAL

Default Real-Time Search Fields
A predefined search can set the default input fields for a real-time search.
You control the optional fields and the required fields that are automatically displayed for real-time
searches. This feature helps you promote data consistency and search effectiveness. For example, XG
requires a name to perform searches. To add an alert to an accept list, an ID or complete address must
be present in the alert. You can set the default fields to require users to provide this information in the
search.
You can set different fields for real-time searches that use a particular predefined search. You can also
configure the predefined search to allow users to add fields for a real-time search.
Related Information
Real-Time Searches on page 36

Set the Default Input Fields for Real-Time Searches
You can configure the default input fields that the predefined search sets for real-time searches.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Default Real-Time Search Fields.

2.

Configure the Name field group in the Individual section:
a. To add a field to the group, click the button for that field.
b. To remove a field from the group, click

(Delete) next to the field name.

c. To require users to provide data in a field, select the check box next to the field name.
d. To display parsed name fields for real-time searches, select Separate Fields.
The First Name field and the Last Name field are displayed for real-time searches. The Middle
Name field and the Generation field are also displayed if they are added to the Name field
group.
e. To display the Full Name field for real-time searches, select Single Full Name Field.
The Full Name field is displayed for real-time searches.
Search results are affected when only a full name is provided.
f. To let the user who performs the search to choose between parsed name fields or the Full Name
field, select Let User Choose.
A Show First Last Name/Show Full Name button is displayed in the Name field group for
real-time searches.
3.

Configure the other field groups in the Individual section:

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 300

CONFIDENTIAL

a. Click Add Fields, and click a field group that you want to add.
Repeat to add additional field groups.
b. To add a field to the group, click the button for that field.
c. To remove a field from the group, click

(Delete) next to the field name.

d. To require users to provide data in a field, select the check box next to the field name.
4.

Configure the field groups in the Business section:
a. Click Add Fields, and click a field group that you want to add.
Repeat to add additional field groups.
b. To add a field to the group, click the button for that field.
c. To remove a field from the group, click

(Delete) next to the field name.

d. To require users to provide data in a field, select the check box next to the field name.
5.

Click Save.

System Values
System values let you customize options in XG in a way that is relevant to your processes. You can create
system values for account types, custom screening list reasons, alert statuses, and decision tags.

Account Types
You can create account types to indicate the type of account that is associated with an input entity.
XG provides default account types that are typical in the finance industry.
You can indicate the account type that an input entity is associated with when you create or edit a batch
format or when you edit account information for an alert.
You can query alerts based on the account type.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 301

CONFIDENTIAL

Custom Screening List Reasons
You can create custom screening list reasons to indicate why records are added to custom screening lists.
XG provides you with several default custom screening list reasons. These default values include reasons
that you can apply to records that are on FinCEN (Financial Crimes Enforcement Network) custom
screening lists.
You can set a custom screening list reason for each record on a custom screening list. You can set the
same custom screening list reason for every record that you import into the list from an import file.
You can query alerts and custom screening list records by the custom screening list reason.

Alert Statuses
You can create alert statuses that users can set in an alert decision to indicate the stage that the alerts
are in as part of your review processes.
You can query the alerts based on their current statuses, their previous statuses, or the date that the
status was changed.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 302

CONFIDENTIAL

You can change the name of most alert statuses. You can also deactivate alert statutes that are no longer
applicable to your review processes. You cannot delete alert statuses.
You cannot change the False Positive status or the Automatic False Positive status. The Automatic False
Positive status is used only by XG to indicate that the input entity meets an Automatic False Positive rule.

Decision Tags
You can create tags that users can set in an alert decision to indicate the reasons for a decision as part of
your review processes. Decision tags can take the place of notes that are manually entered by users each
time they apply an alert decision for more consistent and efficient processes.
You can deactivate decision tags that are no longer applicable to your review processes. You cannot
rename or delete decision tags.

Alert Statuses on page 302

Set Up System Values
You can add account types, custom screening list reasons, alert statuses, and decision tags. You can
change the names of account types and custom screening list reasons. You can deactivate alert statuses
and decision tags.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click System Values.

2.

Click the type of system value that you want to set up:
• Account Types
• Custom Screening List Reasons
• Alert Statuses
• Decision Tags

3.

To add a value, complete the following steps:
a. Click Add Account Type, Add Reason, Add Status, or Add Decision Tag.
b. Enter the value name.
c. Click Save.

4.

To edit a value, click the value, and complete one of the following options:
• For account types or custom screening list reasons, edit the name.
The lock icon ( ) indicates that the system value cannot be changed or deleted.
• For alert statuses and decision tags, clear or click Active.
The lock icon ( ) indicates that the system value cannot be deactivated.

5.

Click Save.

Delete a System Value
You can delete a system value that is no longer applicable to your review processes. You can delete only
account types and custom screening list reasons. You cannot delete alert statuses or decision tags.
Before you begin this task:

Before you delete a system value, you may want to complete one or more of the following tasks:
• Edit queries that contain the system value.
• Query custom screening lists and change any records that contain the custom screening list reason.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click System Values.

2.

Click Account Types or Custom Screening List Reasons.

3.

Click the system value that you want to delete.

4.

Click (Delete).
Deleted system values no longer display as menu options for case management purposes. System
values are not deleted from alerts or custom screening list records.

Related Information
Account Types on page 301
Alert Statuses on page 302
Decision Tags on page 303

Process Settings
Process settings can help you enforce your organization’s review processes. You can set up process
settings that require users to enter notes or to set statuses when they complete certain actions on alerts.
You can also set up process settings that require a user to set all matches in an alert to false positive
before they can set a specified alert status in an alert decision.
Process settings may affect the options that users can apply in alert decisions.
Related Information
Alert Decision Setup on page 293

CONFIDENTIAL

Note Requirements
Notes can help create documentary support during an audit for actions that are performed on an alert.
You can require that users enter notes when they complete the following tasks for alerts:
•
•
•
•
•
•

Change alert states.
Attach files to alerts.
Add alerts to accept lists.
Add alerts to custom screening lists.
Reassign alerts.
Change alert statuses.

Notes are displayed in the Record History section of the Alert View page. Notes are also displayed on
the Record History reports. Notes cannot be deleted. Notes that are provided when alerts are added to
accept lists are displayed in the Comments field of the accept list record.
Related Information
Alert Status Requirements on page 306
Disallowed Status Requirements on page 306
Set Up Process Settings on page 307

Alert Status Requirements
You can require that users set statuses when they reassign alerts or close alerts.
A status can display the stage that the alert is in as part of your review process. You can create system
reports based on the alert status.
Related Information
Note Requirements on page 306
Disallowed Status Requirements on page 306
Set Up Process Settings on page 307

Disallowed Status Requirements
You can set XG to disallow users from setting specified statuses without first indicating that all matches in
an alert are false positives.
For example, you may want users to set a Transaction Approved alert status only after they have
determined that all matches in the alert are false positive.

FIN196-EN_US — 7 September 2023

Bridger Insight XG 5 User Guide Page 306

CONFIDENTIAL

This requirement only affects alert statuses when applying alert decisions to alerts that were generated
from a predefined search that require match decisions.
Related Information
Note Requirements on page 306
Alert Status Requirements on page 306
Set Up Process Settings on page 307

Set Up Process Settings
Process settings let you require users to enter notes or set alert statuses for certain alert actions. Process
settings also let you set XG to disallow the user from setting specified statuses without first indicating all
matches in an alert are false positives.
Procedure:

1.

On the main menu, point to Administration, and click Process Settings.

2.

Select the actions that require users to enter notes or set alert statuses.

3.

Select the alert statuses that require a user to first set all matches in an alert to false positive before
they can set a specified alert status in an alert decision.

4.

Click Save.
